For example, if water and fire stars move together, water can overcome fire, making water the inauspicious star. If water precedes fire, it cannot overcome it. But if fire precedes and water follows, the inauspicious star presses close to the body, causing great harm—this must be carefully examined. The same applies to all stars.

The *Classic* states: "If the inauspicious star precedes and the ruling star follows, one will wield the power of a vassal or minister. If the inauspicious star follows and the ruling star precedes, one will suffer exile or imprisonment."

When stars retrograde, some do so with power, others without. For instance, if fire and metal stars move together and metal precedes while fire follows in retrograde, the inauspicious star dares not advance to overcome metal—this is "retrograde with affection." But if metal retrogrades and encounters fire moving forward, it is "retrograde meeting its inauspicious star." This applies to all five luminaries.

There are also cases where retrograde motion leads to ascending the palace, entering the enclosure, or encountering generation—all auspicious. Conversely, retrograding into a killing star, meeting an inauspicious star, or entering a weak and malevolent palace—all are inauspicious.

Here follows the translation:

---

Among the five stars, the phenomena of *delay*, *station*, *occultation*, and *retrogradation* are of critical importance—scholars must not fail to understand them clearly.

*Delay* means falling behind the proper degree; *station* means halting in motion; *occultation* means becoming invisible; *retrogradation* means moving backward. When a star of beneficial influence moves forward in direct motion, it brings fortune. But when it is *delayed*, *stationary*, *occulted*, or *retrograde*, its power wanes in both advance and retreat.

As the *Classic* states: “In direct motion, one moves with ease; in retrogradation, one shrinks back. When stationary, one is bound and depressed; when occulted, one conceals brilliance and loses radiance.”

For example, if the Life Star is in the *wu* position of the Sun, it is inauspicious when wood-qi occupies the same celestial path. If wood precedes and the Sun follows in retrogradation, misfortune arises; if the Sun precedes and wood follows in retrogradation, fortune ensues.

When a star of beneficial influence is *stationary* in a substantial position, its fortune endures. But if an inauspicious star is *stationary* in a substantial position, its misfortune persists without cease. If *stationary* in an insubstantial position, neither fortune nor misfortune arises.

When a star of beneficial influence is *occulted*, its power weakens; when an inauspicious star is *occulted*, no disaster occurs.

*Retrogradation* is backward motion. Some retrogradations bring fortune, others misfortune—this must be determined by reasoned analysis.

As the *Verse* says:
> When the five stars meet the Sun, they must occult;
> When three meet in yang, they surely station.
> If in opposition they form retrograde motion,
> Where yang is absent, there is delay.

The *Luoji* and *Jidu* stars sever the celestial dome, bringing both fortune and misfortune. If they sever stars to the left while the life limit moves to the right, this is called “turning away.” Since the life limit does not encounter the stars, outcomes vary in ascent and descent.

If during the day the stars occupy the sky and the severance occurs in the *chen-si-wu-wei-shen* positions with stars present, while the life limit moves through the *you-xu-hai-zi-chou-yin* positions without stars, this is called “failing to attain embodiment.” Similarly, if at night the severance occurs in the *xu-hai-zi-chou-yin* positions with stars present, while the life limit moves through the *chen-si-wu-wei-shen* positions without stars, these too reflect differing ascents and descents and do not conform to proper patterns.

When the *Luoji* and *Jidu* sever the celestial dome, if one star leaps beyond the Dipper, its fortune or misfortune must be assessed independently. If the leaping star is a fortune lord, emolument lord, life lord, body lord, or a star of official rank, authority, or nobility—such as night fire, night moon, day wood, or day earth—this is considered a proper pattern, and the native will surely attain wealth, honor, and success.

But if the leaping star is one of punishment, imprisonment, or hidden depletion, or a star of servitude, the *yangren*, *jiesha*, or *dishe*, or day fire, day metal, or night earth, and it escapes outward, these do not conform to proper patterns. Such natives will surely endure poverty, toil, and hardship, passing through life without achievement, and cannot be deemed fortunate.

The severance must not allow the Sun to leap outward. If the Sun is isolated externally, this is called “the solitary ruler.” A ruler in solitary retreat without assistance is extremely inauspicious. Since the Sun symbolizes the sovereign, it must be accompanied by assisting stars, preferably with auspicious stars to its left and right. If the Sun stands alone, even close attendants will distance themselves, and the native will surely suffer hardship.

When stars gather in conjunction, some gatherings are auspicious, others inauspicious. Auspicious gatherings involve the life lord, body lord, palace lord, official rank, fortune, or emolument, or transformations into authority, nobility, or protective seals—all are auspicious. Even if the gathering includes fire, *Luoji*, *Jidu*, or *Beidou*, no harm arises.

But if the gathering does not involve the aforementioned stars and instead includes the *dishe*, *jiesha*, *yangren*, or other malevolent stars, or transforms into punishment, imprisonment, or hidden depletion, it is inauspicious. Scholars must not fail to discern this.

When the life or body lord occupies the position of servants, outcomes may be either auspicious or inauspicious. In the charts of noble persons, the life or body lord often enters the servant position and still attains nobility, though some enter it and remain base.

If the servant palace originally occupies a position of nobility, emolument, *changsheng*, *diwang*, rank, merit, authority, or emolument, the native will surely attain wealth, honor, and success. But if the servant palace originally occupies a position of *jiesha*, *dishe*, *yangren*, *sijue*, or *baobai*, and the life or body lord resides there, the native will surely be one who toils without achievement. Scholars must examine this with great care.

In constructing a life chart, the four cardinal positions are of paramount importance. If the Sun and Moon illuminate the four cardinals, or if metal and wood illuminate them, or if fortune and virtue illuminate them, or if the star of beneficial influence occupies the four cardinal positions, the native will surely attain wealth and honor. Even if fire, *Luoji*, *Jidu*, or *Beidou* guard the four strong positions and transform favorably, this is also considered proper.

But if stars of punishment, imprisonment, or hidden depletion occupy the four cardinal palaces and encounter clashing stars, the native will surely suffer ruin and defeat.

In examining the stars, one follows the same method as in life analysis: consider both the three harmonies and direct illumination to determine fortune or misfortune. Generally, in assessing the three harmonies and four auxiliaries, the five stars are given less weight than direct illumination. The four auxiliaries are emphasized over the five stars, for the four auxiliaries are stars of sudden, disruptive force.

When the ten celestial stems govern life, as in a *jia* year, one must not establish life in the degree of a metal constellation—this is called “ghostly clash” and brings misfortune. It is auspicious only to sit on a star of generation in a water constellation—this is called “upon the parents.” Sitting on an earth constellation is called “upon wealth and silk.” Sitting on a fire constellation is called “upon release from entanglement.” One must intuitively grasp the waxing and waning of influence; being timely and in accord with the season is most excellent. The rest follow this principle.

When life or body sits on emolument, nobility, *changsheng*, the storehouse, the chariot, the palace, the encircling noble nest, the pivot of emolument and horses, or the palaces of *sheng* and *wang*, the native will surely attain wealth and honor. Even if not fully so, they will still enjoy ample clothing and food.

As the *Tianxuan Fu* states:
> When emolument, horses, and noble persons hold the world and establish the body,
> One must attain purity and high rank.
> When inauspicious stars and killers approach the body,
> One’s conduct will surely be base and lowly.

When life or body sits on *jieshe*, *yangren*, *baobai*, emptiness, *sijue*, the three killers, or the *Feilian* killer, the native will surely be treacherous, eccentric, unfilial, unrighteous, violent, and toilsome.

When life or body is flanked by the Sun and Moon, by *fude* (fortune and virtue), by *guankui* (official prominence), by *yingui* (seal and nobility), or by the three harmonies converging upon them, all are auspicious. Even if the life ruler or body ruler arises in another location yet still flanks and converges upon them, all remain auspicious.

When the palace of *jieshe* (robbery) or *mangren* (blades) is flanked by inauspicious stars, their baleful consequences are beyond description. Yet without *guanfu* (official talismans), blades cannot form; without *suipo* (annual destruction), robbery cannot arise; without *bingfu* (illness talismans), sickness and misfortune cannot take shape—such is the true generation and destruction of the five phases.

The palace of official emolument must not be afflicted by star clashes; such a palace is called *guangui* (official ghost). For instance, if official emolument resides in the *yin* (Tiger) position, one must not allow the Metal star to enter it, nor should the three harmonies or four cardinal palaces occupy it—all such configurations portend litigation, official entanglements, or the absence of emolument.

The palaces of official emolument and *fude* (fortune and virtue) most require the presence of auspicious stars. If the Sun and Moon reside in the palace of official emolument or *fude*, or if *fulu* (fortune and emolument) resides in the palaces of office or fortune, or if Water, Sun, Metal, or Moon each occupy the palace of official emolument, and the moving limit encounters them, all portend the flourishing of fortune. If the palaces of office and fortune lack stars but are activated by auspicious luminaries suspended above them, this too is auspicious. One must also examine the opposing and triply harmonizing palaces to determine fortune or misfortune.

In constructing a destiny, one need only seek the ruling star, the life degree, the life ruler, the body degree, and the body ruler, assessing their strength, weakness, fortune, and misfortune—there is no need for every star to be exalted or in its proper place. Thus the *Classic* states: "If one star is well-placed, one will be noble and auspicious throughout life." It also says: "If one star is adverse and its faults are not examined, even if all other luminaries are auspicious, they cannot bring fortune." For example, among five or seven officials in office, not every one need be competent; if but one is capable, all underlings in the prefectures and counties will regard him with respect.

In observing the stars, one must first apply reason, then examine the limit ruler and the moving limit. The limit ruler must be exalted, well-placed, and receiving the convergence of life-giving auspicious stars to constitute a good limit and bring success. Otherwise, all are inauspicious.

In discussing the five stars, one must investigate the celestial lodgings of the Sun and Moon to determine fortune and misfortune, wealth and poverty, nobility and baseness—nine out of ten will be accurate. For the life palace, the Sun is the ruler; for the body palace, the Moon is the ruler. When the root is upright, what foundation is lacking? Thus, by day one must examine the Sun, and by night the Moon. If by day the Sun encounters baleful stars, or by night the Moon encounters inauspicious stars, the native will surely suffer poverty, lowliness, and early death. If by day auspicious constellations meet the Sun, or by night the stars hook the Moon, the native will surely enjoy wealth, nobility, and prominence. Yet one must still consider whether they are within their proper degrees or not.

If all stars are gentle and yielding, they cannot accomplish great deeds; one must have a baleful star to augment their authority. Generally, if auspicious stars are many and baleful stars few, one judges by the auspicious. If baleful stars are many and auspicious stars few, one judges by the baleful. In the destiny of a noble person, without the power of baleful stars, they cannot govern the world.

In all destinies, the Sun and Moon must be bright and pure to be considered auspicious. Heaven and Earth take the Sun and Moon as their rulers; only when the Sun and Moon are bright can one attain nobility and prominence. The *Classic* states: "For a noble person, the Sun and Moon must be distinct; if the Sun and Moon are not bright, they are not noble."

While the original guarding star may be good, one must still fear the harm of stars in the flowing years. If the limit ruler is both baleful and weak, and the flowing year’s baleful stars are heavy, they too can bring disaster—this must not be overlooked. If the limit ruler is strong, and only the flowing year brings misfortune, one must wait until the baleful stars depart before improvement comes. Thus the *Classic* states: "Though the original guard may be blameless, one still fears calamity in the flowing year; though the original guard may be pure, it surpasses the savor of fine food, while the flowing year’s misfortune is like rootless floodwaters." Therefore, those who wish to make good choices must ensure that the original guarding star was once auspicious and the limit ruler is not debilitated or weak before employing them.

*Rumen Chongli Zhezhong Kanyu Wanxiao Lu*, Scroll Three, concludes.

*Rumen Chongli Zhezhong Kanyu Wanxiao Lu*, Scroll Four: *Seven Governors* (Excerpt)

The *Seven Governors* refer to the Sun, the Moon, Jupiter, Mars, Saturn, Venus, and Mercury. All auspicious or inauspicious orientations in mountain geomancy derive from these. The method requires first examining the flow of celestial qi to discern the waxing and waning of its transformations; next, observing the heavens to distinguish the stars; and then inspecting the earth to differentiate the terrestrial correspondences. Thus, one may pursue the auspicious and avoid the inauspicious—this is the essential mechanism of divination. A detailed exposition follows.

**Application of the Seven Governors**
The Sun is the essence of fire and the most auspicious spirit; it bestows blessings, not misfortune, except during solar eclipses, when it is highly inauspicious.

The Moon is the essence of water, secondary to the Sun; it also bestows blessings, not misfortune, except during lunar eclipses, when it is inauspicious.

Jupiter, called the Year Star, exerts urgent influence over fortune and misfortune in winter and spring, but its effects are delayed in summer and autumn.

Mars, called the Sparkling Deluder, exerts urgent influence in spring and summer, but its effects are delayed in autumn and winter.

Saturn, called the Quelling Star, exerts urgent influence during the four seasons, but its effects are delayed in spring and autumn.

Venus, called the Great White, exerts urgent influence in the final months of the seasons and in autumn, but its effects are delayed in summer and winter.

Mercury, called the Chronographic Star, exerts urgent influence in autumn and winter, but its effects are delayed in spring and summer.

Qi is the surplus of wood, its fortune and misfortune secondary to Jupiter.

Comets are the surplus of water, their fortune and misfortune secondary to Mercury.

Rahu is the surplus of fire, its fortune and misfortune secondary to Mars.

Ketu is the surplus of earth, its fortune and misfortune secondary to Saturn.

The lunar lodges *Xing*, *Xu*, *Fang*, and *Mao* are the palaces traversed by the Sun.

The lodges *Zhang*, *Wei*, *Xin*, and *Bi* are the palaces traversed by the Moon.

The lodges *Jiao*, *Dou*, *Kui*, and *Jing* are the palaces traversed by Jupiter.

The lodges *Wei*, *Shi*, *Zi*, and *Yi* are the palaces traversed by Mars.

The lodges *Shi*, *Nü*, *Wei*, and *Liu* are the palaces traversed by Saturn.

The lodges *Kang*, *Niu*, *Lou*, and *Gui* are the palaces traversed by Venus.

The lodges *Ji*, *Bi*, *Shen*, and *Wo* are the palaces traversed by Mercury.

These are the degrees through which the Seven Governors move. Encountering generative or supportive influences brings auspiciousness; encountering destructive or draining influences brings misfortune.

**Diagram of Yin-Yang and the Five Phases**
This is the fixed structure of yin-yang and the Five Phases, derived from the numbers of the *River Chart*, all based on the earthly branches. The twelve celestial stems occupy their positions but do not govern their qi exclusively; one must calculate from right to left.

**Diagram of the Fixed Human Element**
The celestial stems are called the Heavenly Element, the earthly branches the Earthly Element. What is concealed within the branches is called the Human Element—indispensable for those engaged in fate calculation and divination. The details are illustrated in the following verse:

Within the *Zi* palace, *Gui* water resides;
*Zi* and *Chou* share *Gui*, *Xin* metal, and *Ji* earth.
The *Yin* palace holds *Jia* wood, *Bing* fire, and *Wu* earth;
The *Mao* palace, *Yi* wood alone, thrives in abundance.
The *Chen* palace divides *Yi* wood, *Wu* earth, and *Gui* water;
The *Si* palace gathers *Ji* earth, *Geng* metal, and *Bing* fire.
The *Wu* palace contains *Ding* fire and *Ji* earth;
The *Wei* palace unites *Yi* wood, *Ji* earth, and *Ding* fire.
The *Shen* palace holds *Ren* water, *Geng* metal, and *Wu* earth;
The *You* palace follows *Xin* metal and *Geng* metal.
Only the *Xu* palace combines *Ding* fire, *Xin* metal, and *Wu* earth;
The *Hai* palace’s true lineage is *Ren* water and *Jia* wood.

**Diagram of the Life and Death of the Five Phases**
*Long Life*, *Bathing*, *Coming of Age*, *Officership*, *Flourishing*, *Decline*, *Illness*, *Death*, *Grave*, *Extinction*, *Embryo*, and *Nurturing*—these follow in sequence. Yang moves forward, yin moves backward; when yang dies, yin must live, and when yin dies, yang must live.

*Embryo* and *Nurturing* are advancing qi; *Coming of Age* and *Officership* are flourishing qi; *Bathing* is waning qi; *Decline* and *Illness* are retreating qi; *Grave* is storing qi; *Death* and *Extinction* are exhausted qi.

Generally, advancing qi does not bring death, nor does retreating qi bring life. Yet there are cases of survival in death and rebirth in extinction—these are matters a fate calculator must not overlook.

**Diagram of the Generation and Conquest of the Five Phases**
This is the *River Chart*: Heaven One generates water, Earth Six completes it; Earth Two generates fire, Heaven Seven completes it; Heaven Three generates wood, Earth Eight completes it; Earth Four generates metal, Heaven Nine completes it; Heaven Five generates earth, Earth Ten completes it. Each generates and conquers—such is the natural nature of the Five Phases. If one engaged in divination understands their generative and conquering nature and practices the Way of regulation and transformation, there will be no excess or deficiency. How could this not suffice to pursue the auspicious and avoid the inauspicious?

**Diagram of the Sun’s Rising and Setting**
Modern astrologers claim the Sun rises in *Mao* and sets in *You*—this is merely an approximation. For precise divination, one must consult this diagram to determine the exact time.

**Diagram of the Moon’s Dawn and Dusk**
Almanacs record that after the new moon, the Moon’s degrees are measured at dusk, and after the full moon, at dawn—this, too, is an approximation. For accurate divination, one must consult this diagram to ensure the timing is correct.

**Diagram of the Stars’ Terrestrial Correspondences**
These are the terrestrial correspondences that align with the celestial stars. Those engaged in divination must not be ignorant of them, nor should those observing celestial qi.

**Diagram of the Transiting Constellations**
This is the fixed arrangement of the Twenty-Eight Lodges and the sequence of the Seven Governors’ movements. Their correspondence to the twelve terrestrial regions must not be overlooked.

**Diagram of the Fixed Positions of the Stars**
Each palace contains slightly more than thirty degrees, totaling 365¼ degrees—the fractional remainders of each palace. When examining the Seven Governors, one assigns them to the twelve palaces according to this diagram, which also serves as the basis for determining the positions of the *Nobleman*, *Salary*, and *Horse*. For example, *Gui*’s salary is in *Zi*; one checks where Saturn resides to find the salary’s origin, and the rest follow accordingly. The Four Surpluses are assessed based on their governing qi.

Three degrees of *Shi* enter *Mao*, three degrees of *Wei* enter *Yin*;
Four degrees of *Dou* are sought within *Chou*;
Two degrees of *Nü* have passed, then *Xu* turns;
Thirteen degrees of *Wei* revolve within *Hai*.

**Diagram of the Degrees of the Celestial Sphere**
*Kui* enters *Xu* by two degrees, *Wei* enters *You* by four;
*Bi* shifts past *Shen* by seven degrees;
*Jing* passes *Wei* by nine, *Liu* enters *Wu* by four;
*Zhang* extends into *Si* by fifteen, *Zhen* reaches *Chen* by ten.

**Diagram of the Enclosures and Configurations of the Stars**
Whenever a *wei*-star resides in the palace of its governing *qi* and occupies the degree of its own *qi*, it is called *dwelling in the enclosure*. When it resides in the palace of its generating *qi* and occupies the degree of its generating *qi*, it is called *entering the configuration*. When it resides in the palace of its own *qi* but occupies the degree of its generating *qi*, it is called *dwelling in the enclosure and entering the configuration*. When it resides in the palace of its generating *qi* but occupies the degree of its own *qi*, it is called *entering the configuration and dwelling in the enclosure*. The fortunes and misfortunes of such stars are of utmost importance, and their activation is equivalent to that of the ruling star.

**Method of Degrees**
The celestial sphere comprises 365¼ degrees. Whenever "a quarter of a degree" is mentioned, it refers to twenty-five *fen*. For one degree equals one hundred *fen*, and one *fen* equals one hundred *miao*. All ancient and modern calendrical methods are calculated accordingly.

**Fixed Configuration of the Celestial Motion by Hour**
Each *ke* advances slightly more than three degrees—precisely three degrees and seventy-six *fen*. Each hour traverses one palace and a fraction, totaling thirty degrees and fifty-one *fen*, thirty-three *miao*, and a fraction. In one day, it completes 365¼ degrees and advances by one additional degree. Compared to the sun’s motion, it exceeds by one degree; compared to the moon’s motion, it exceeds by thirteen degrees. After one year, it completes the full cycle of the celestial sphere, reunites with the sun, and marks the end of the year. Some say the celestial motion completes one revolution in a year, referring only to the degrees it advances.

**Fixed Configuration of the Sun’s Motion by Hour**
Each *ke* advances slightly more than three degrees—precisely three degrees and seventy-five *fen*. Each hour advances one palace, totaling thirty degrees and forty-three *fen*, seventy-five *miao*, and a fraction. In one day, it completes 365¼ degrees, falling short of the celestial motion by nearly one degree and exceeding the moon’s motion by twelve degrees. In one year, it does not complete a full revolution of the celestial sphere. At the winter solstice, it moves through degrees of excess; at the summer solstice, through degrees of deficiency. Though the excess and deficiency differ, calendrical experts generally calculate by subtracting one degree per day.

**Fixed Configuration of the Moon’s Motion by Hour**
Each *ke* advances slightly more than three degrees—precisely three degrees and fifty *fen*. Each hour advances slightly less than one palace, totaling twenty-nine degrees and forty-three *fen*, seventy-five *miao*, and a fraction. In one day, it completes 353¼ degrees, falling short of the sun’s motion by twelve degrees and the celestial motion by thirteen degrees. In twenty-nine days, it completes a full revolution of the celestial sphere, marking the new moon. Before the quarter moon, its retreat is swift; after the quarter moon, its retreat slows. On average, it retreats by thirteen degrees and thirty-seven *fen* per day.

**Fixed Configuration of Jupiter’s Motion by Hour**
Each hour advances slightly more than one palace, totaling slightly more than thirty degrees, falling short of the celestial motion by slightly more than seventy *miao*. In one day, it completes 365¼ degrees and advances by slightly less than one degree, falling short of the celestial motion by thirty-three *miao* and a fraction. In twelve days, it falls short by one degree; in one hundred twenty days, by ten degrees; in three hundred sixty days, by one palace. In twelve years, it completes a full revolution of the celestial sphere.

**Fixed Configuration of Mars’ Motion by Hour**
Each hour advances slightly more than one palace, totaling slightly more than thirty degrees, falling short of the celestial motion by four *fen* and slightly less than seventy *miao*. In one day, it completes 365 degrees and advances by slightly less than one degree, falling short of the celestial motion by fifty *fen*. In two days, it falls short by one degree; in sixty days, by one palace. In two years, it completes a full revolution of the celestial sphere.

**Fixed Configuration of Saturn’s Motion by Hour (Same as the *Qi*-Star)**
Each hour advances slightly more than one palace, totaling slightly more than thirty degrees, falling short of the celestial motion by twenty-nine *miao* and five-tenths of a *miao*. In one day, it completes 365¼ degrees and advances by slightly less than one degree, falling short of the celestial motion by slightly less than three *fen* and fifty-three *miao*. In twenty-eight days, five hours, one *ke*, and six *fen*, it falls short by one degree. In two hundred eighty days and four hours, it falls short by ten degrees and twenty *fen*. In one month and twenty-five days, it falls short by one palace. In twenty-eight years, it completes a full revolution of the celestial sphere.

**Fixed Configuration of Venus and Mercury’s Motion by Hour**
Each hour advances one palace and a fraction, totaling slightly more than thirty degrees, falling short of the celestial motion by eight *fen* and thirty-three *miao*. In one day, it completes slightly less than 365¼ degrees, falling short of the celestial motion by slightly more than one degree. In one month, it falls short by one palace; in one year, it completes a full revolution of the celestial sphere.

**Fixed Configuration of the Purple *Qi*’s Motion by Hour**
The configuration of this star’s motion should be inferred from that of Saturn, as it also completes a full revolution of the celestial sphere in twenty-eight years.

**Fixed Configuration of the Moon’s *Bei*’s Motion by Hour**
Each hour advances slightly more than twenty-nine degrees and ninety-nine *fen*, falling short of the celestial motion by slightly less than one *fen*. In one day, it completes 365¼ degrees and advances by eighty-eight *fen*, falling short of the celestial motion by slightly less than twelve *fen*. In nine days, it falls short by one degree; in ninety days, by ten degrees; in nine months, by one palace. In nine years, it completes a full revolution of the celestial sphere.

**Fixed Configuration of *Luo* and *Ji*’s Motion by Hour**
Each hour moves in retrograde by one palace and nine *fen*, fifty *miao*, and a fraction, falling short of the celestial motion by slightly more than fifty *miao*. In one day, it moves in retrograde by 365¼ degrees and advances by slightly more than ninety-four *fen*.

It falls short of the celestial motion by slightly less than six *fen*. In eighteen days, it falls short by one degree; in one hundred eighty days, by ten degrees; in eighteen months, by one palace. In eighteen years, it completes a full revolution of the celestial sphere. Calendarists calculate based on its retrograde motion, hence the saying: "*Luo* and *Ji* revolve leftward, while the Seven Luminaries, *qi*, and comets all turn rightward."

In selecting years, months, days, and hours, one must sequentially track the Seven Luminaries, *qi*, and comets while retrogradely tracking the two stars *Luo* and *Ji*. Otherwise, misfortune will surely follow—this cannot be neglected.

**Fixed Configuration of the Imperial Star’s Motion by Hour**
Each hour, it advances by one-twelfth of a degree. In one day, it moves forward by one degree; in one month, by one palace; in one year, it completes a full revolution of the celestial sphere.

The calendar begins at the *Jingzhe* solar term, with the hour at *jia*, moving sequentially toward *mao*. Each node passes one mountain—arriving at the mountain is most auspicious. Whether reaching the orientation, the three directions, or the four cardinal points, if they assist or support me, it is auspicious; if they restrain or drain me, it is inauspicious.

Master Yang said: "Building in spring is auspicious in the east; in summer, in the south; in autumn, in the west; in winter, in the north. During the four seasons, building in the four corners is auspicious—does this not reflect the same principle?" In spring, it is called the Green Emperor; in summer, the Red Emperor; in autumn, the White Emperor; in winter, the Black Emperor. Though their names differ with the seasons, the principle remains one.

**Fixed Configuration of Auspicious and Inauspicious Palaces and Degrees**
The *zi* and *chou* palaces, along with the *Bing*, *Nü*, *Wei*, and *Liu* lodges, are all positions of earth. For those residing above them, wood-*qi* is harmful, water-comets are adversaries, fire-*Luo* is benevolent, and metal is useful—these are the ruling stars in the four seasonal months.

The *yin* and *hai* palaces, along with the *Jiao*, *Dou*, *Kui*, and *Jing* lodges, are all positions of wood. For those residing above them, metal is harmful, earth-*Ji* is an adversary, water-comets are benevolent, and fire-*Luo* is useful—these are the ruling stars in spring.

The *mao* and *xu* palaces, along with the *Wei*, *Shi*, *Zi*, and *Yi* lodges, are all positions of fire. For those residing above them, water-comets are harmful, metal is an adversary, wood-*qi* is benevolent, and earth-*Ji* is useful—these are the ruling stars in summer.

The *chen* and *you* palaces, along with the *Kang*, *Niu*, *Lou*, and *Gui* lodges, are all positions of metal. For those residing above them, fire-*Luo* is harmful, wood-*qi* is an adversary, earth-*Ji* is benevolent, and water-comets are useful—these are the ruling stars in autumn.

The *si* and *shen* palaces, along with the *Ji*, *Bi*, *Shen*, and *Gang* lodges, are all positions of water. For those residing above them, earth-*Ji* is harmful, fire-*Luo* is an adversary, metal is benevolent, and wood-*qi* is useful—these are the ruling stars in winter.

The *wu* palace, along with the *Xing*, *Xu*, *Fang*, and *Xu* lodges, is the position of the Great Yang. For those residing above it, the conjunction of fire-*Luo* and wood is inauspicious; metal and water stars are favored. It is suitable for daytime but not for night, and a solar eclipse is inauspicious.

The *wei* palace, along with the *Zhang*, *Wei*, *Xin*, and *Bi* lodges, is the position of the Great Yin. For those residing above it, the conjunction of earth-*Ji* is inauspicious; metal and water stars are also favored. It is suitable for night but not for day, stronger before the full moon and weaker after. A lunar eclipse is inauspicious.

In the above palace degrees, benevolent and useful stars in their season are auspicious, while adversarial and harmful stars in their season are highly inauspicious. This principle applies not only to each palace but also to major and minor limits—all follow this rule.

**Diagrammatic Explanation**
The twenty-eight lunar lodges are distributed across the twelve palaces, forming the sequence of the Seven Governors’ motion. The seven governors and four remnants move through each year, giving rise to celestial changes. Two diagrams follow for easy reference.

Where the Great Yang resides determines the life palace (*ming*); where the Great Yin resides determines the body palace (*shen*). Once life and body are established, the ruling stars of each palace can be deduced. For example:
- If *ming* is in *zi* and earth is the ruler, wealth is in *hai*;
- If wood is the ruler, siblings are in *xu*;
- If fire is the ruler, property is in *you*;
- If metal is the ruler, children are in *shen*;
- If water is the ruler, servants are in *wei*;
- If the moon is the ruler, the spouse palace is in *wu*;
- If the sun is the ruler, illness is in *si*;
- If water is the ruler, relocation is in *chen*;
- If metal is the ruler, official rank is in *mao*;
- If fire is the ruler, fortune and virtue are in *yin*;
- If wood is the ruler, appearance is in *chou*;
- If earth is the ruler, yearly celestial and terrestrial stars all derive from this.

If scholars can consult the diagrams, they may discern fortune and misfortune, mastering the art of selection.

**Sequence of the Twelve Palaces**
For nighttime hours, count from the body palace (*shen*).
1. Life Palace (*minggong*)
2. Wealth
3. Siblings
4. Property
5. Children
6. Servants
7. Spouse
8. Illness
9. Relocation
10. Official Rank
11. Fortune and Virtue
12. Appearance

**Strengths and Weaknesses of the Twelve Palaces**
Strong palaces: Life, Spouse, Property and Wealth, Official Rank and Fortune, Children.
Weak palaces: Relocation, Illness, Servants, Siblings.
Those aligned with the season are exceptions.

**Life and Body Palaces in the Twelve Palaces**
From *mao* to *you* is daytime, so count from the life palace (*minggong*):
1. Life Palace
2. Wealth
3. Siblings
...and so on, retrograding through the twelve palaces.

From *you* to *mao* is nighttime, so count from the body palace (*shengong*):
1. Body Palace
2. Wealth
3. Siblings
...also retrograding through the twelve palaces.

Even for the seven strong palaces, nighttime uses the body palace, and daytime uses the life palace—this is the correct method. Moreover, the life and body palaces each have their ruling stars and degree rulers, which those who practice selection must not overlook.

**Annotations for Each Palace Degree**

**Zi Palace Degree**
In heaven, it belongs to the *Xuanxiao* lunar lodge; on earth, its terrestrial correlate is Qi.
For those whose life or body palace resides here, earth is the palace ruler (*gongzhu*). Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If the life or body palace occupies *Wei* (Danger) constellation, the moon (*Taiyin*) governs the degree ruler (*duzhu*). Favor metal and water, avoid earth and *Ji*. Inauspicious on moonless nights; auspicious when luminous.
- If occupying *Xu* (Void) constellation, the sun (*Taiyang*) governs the degree ruler. Avoid fire, *Luo*, and wood stars; favor metal and water in harmony. Inauspicious at night; auspicious by day.
- If occupying *Nü* (Woman) constellation, earth governs the degree ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens align with the palace ruler.

**Chou Palace Degree**
In heaven, it belongs to the *Xingji* lunar lodge; on earth, its terrestrial correlate is Wu.
For those whose life or body palace resides here, earth is the palace ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If the life or body palace occupies *Nü* (Woman) constellation, earth governs the degree ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens align with the palace ruler.
- If occupying *Niu* (Ox) constellation, metal governs the degree ruler. Fire and *Luo* are adversities; wood *qi* is hostile; earth and *Ji* are beneficent; water and *Bei* are useful.
- If occupying *Dou* (Dipper) constellation, wood governs the degree ruler. Metal is adversity; earth and *Ji* are hostile; water and *Bei* are beneficent; fire and *Luo* are useful.

**Yin Palace Degree**
In heaven, it belongs to the *Ximu* lunar lodge; on earth, its terrestrial correlate is Yan.
For those whose life or body palace resides here, wood is the palace ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If the life or body palace occupies *Niu* (Ox) constellation, wood governs the degree ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens align with the palace ruler.
- If occupying *Ji* (Winnowing Basket) constellation, water governs the degree ruler. Earth and *Ji* are adversities; fire and *Luo* are hostile; metal is beneficent; wood *qi* is useful.
- If occupying *Wei* (Tail) constellation, fire governs the degree ruler. Water and *Bei* are adversities; metal is hostile; wood *qi* is beneficent; earth and *Ji* are useful.

**Mao Palace Degree**
In heaven, it belongs to the *Dahuo* lunar lodge; on earth, its terrestrial correlate is Song.
For those whose life or body palace resides here, fire is the palace ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If the life or body palace occupies *Wei* (Tail) constellation, favorable and unfavorable omens align with the palace ruler.
- If occupying *Xin* (Heart) constellation, the moon (*Taiyin*) governs the degree ruler. Favor metal and water, avoid earth and *Ji*. Inauspicious on moonless nights; auspicious when luminous.
- If occupying *Fang* (Room) constellation, the sun (*Taiyang*) governs the degree ruler. Avoid fire, *Luo*, and wood stars; favor metal and water in harmony. Inauspicious at night; auspicious by day.
- If occupying *Di* (Root) constellation, earth governs the degree ruler. Wood *qi* is adversity; water and *Bei* are hostile; fire and *Luo* are beneficent; metal is useful.

**Chen Palace Degree**
In heaven, it belongs to the *Shouxing* lunar lodge; on earth, its terrestrial correlate is Zheng.
For those whose life or body palace resides here, metal is the palace ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If the life or body palace occupies *Di* (Root) constellation, earth governs the degree ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If occupying *Kang* (Neck) constellation, metal governs the degree ruler. Fire and *Luo* are adversities; wood *qi* is hostile; earth and *Ji* are beneficent; water and *Bei* are useful.
- If occupying *Jiao* (Horn) constellation, wood governs the degree ruler. Metal is adversity; earth is hostile; water and *Bei* are beneficent; fire and *Luo* are useful.
- If occupying *Zhen* (Wing) constellation, water governs the degree ruler. Earth and *Ji* are adversities; fire and *Luo* are hostile; metal is beneficent; wood *qi* is useful.

**Si Palace Degree**
In heaven, it belongs to the *Chunwei* lunar lodge; on earth, its terrestrial correlate is Chu.
For those whose life or body palace resides here, water is the palace ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If the life or body palace occupies *Yi* (Wings) constellation, fire governs the degree ruler. Water and *Bei* are adversities; metal is hostile; wood *qi* is beneficent; earth and *Ji* are useful.
- If occupying *Zhang* (Extended Net) constellation, the moon (*Taiyin*) governs the degree ruler. Favor metal and water, avoid earth and *Ji*. Inauspicious on moonless nights; auspicious when luminous.

**Wu Palace Degree**
In heaven, it belongs to the *Chunhuo* lunar lodge; on earth, its terrestrial correlate is Zhou.
For those whose life or body palace resides here, the sun (*Taiyang*) is the palace ruler. Avoid fire, *Luo*, and wood stars; favor metal and water in harmony. Inauspicious at night; auspicious by day.
- If the life or body palace occupies *Zhang* (Extended Net) constellation, the moon (*Taiyin*) governs the degree ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as stated above.
- If occupying *Xing* (Star) constellation, the sun (*Taiyang*) governs the degree ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens align with the palace ruler.
- If occupying *Liu* (Willow) constellation, earth governs the degree ruler. Wood *qi* is adversity; water and *Bei* are hostile; fire and *Luo* are beneficent; metal is useful.

**Wei Palace Degree**
In heaven, it belongs to the *Chunshou* lunar lodge; on earth, its terrestrial correlate is Qin.
For those whose life or body palace resides here, the moon (*Taiyin*) is the palace ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If the life or body palace occupies *Liu* (Willow) constellation, earth governs the degree ruler. Wood *qi* is adversity; water and *Bei* are hostile; fire and *Luo* are beneficent; metal is useful.
- If occupying *Gui* (Ghost) constellation, metal governs the degree ruler. Fire and *Luo* are adversities; wood *qi* is hostile; earth and *Ji* are beneficent; water and *Bei* are useful.
- If occupying *Jing* (Well) constellation, wood governs the degree ruler. Metal is adversity; earth and *Ji* are hostile; water and *Bei* are beneficent; fire and *Luo* are useful.

**Shen Palace Degree**
In heaven, it belongs to the *Shichen* lunar lodge; on earth, its terrestrial correlate is Jin.
For those whose life or body palace resides here, water is the palace ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If the life or body palace occupies *Jing* (Well) constellation, wood governs the degree ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If occupying *Shen* (Triaster) constellation, water governs the degree ruler. Earth and *Ji* are adversities; fire and *Luo* are hostile; metal is beneficent; wood *qi* is useful.
- If occupying *Zi* (Turtle Beak) constellation, fire governs the degree ruler. Water and *Bei* are adversities; metal is hostile; wood *qi* is beneficent; earth and *Ji* are useful.
- If occupying *Bi* (Net) constellation, the moon (*Taiyin*) governs the degree ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.

---
**You Palace Degrees**
In heaven, this belongs to the *Daliang* lunar lodge; on earth, its corresponding terrestrial region is Zhao. For those whose life or body palace resides here, metal is the palace ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If the life or body palace occupies *Bi* (Net) constellation, favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If occupying *Xu* constellation, the sun (*Taiyang*) governs the degree ruler. Hostile to fire, *Luo*, and Jupiter; favors metal and water in mutual containment. Inauspicious at night, auspicious by day.
- If occupying *Wei* (Stomach) constellation, earth governs the degree ruler. Wood *qi* is adversity; water and *Bei* are hostile; fire and *Luo* are beneficent; metal is useful.

**Xu Palace Degrees**
In heaven, this belongs to the *Jianglou* lunar lodge; on earth, its corresponding terrestrial region is Lu. For those whose life palace resides here, fire is the life ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If the life or body palace occupies *Wei* (Stomach) constellation, earth governs the ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If occupying *Lou* (Harvester) constellation, metal governs the degree ruler. Fire and *Luo* are adversities; wood *qi* is hostile; earth and *Ji* are beneficent; water and *Bei* are useful.
- If occupying *Kui* (Straddler) constellation, wood governs the degree ruler. Metal is adversity; earth and *Ji* are hostile; water and *Bei* are beneficent; fire and *Luo* are useful.

**Hai Palace Degrees**
In heaven, this belongs to the *Zouzi* lunar lodge; on earth, its corresponding terrestrial region is Wei. For those whose life or body palace resides here, wood is the palace ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If the life or body palace occupies *Kui* (Straddler) constellation, wood governs the degree ruler. Favorable and unfavorable omens are as previously stated.
- If occupying *Bi* (Wall) constellation, water governs the degree ruler. Earth and *Ji* are adversities; fire and *Luo* are hostile; metal is beneficent; wood is useful.
- If occupying *Shi* (House) constellation, fire governs the degree ruler. Water and *Bei* are adversities; metal is hostile; wood *qi* is beneficent; earth and *Ji* are useful.
- If occupying *Wei* (Rooftop) constellation, the moon (*Taiyin*) governs the degree ruler. Favors metal and water; disfavors earth and *Ji*. Inauspicious on moonless nights, auspicious when luminous.

Some contemporary practitioners of astrological fate-calculation emphasize only the palace ruler, while others focus solely on the degree ruler—neither is a definitive principle. For true insight, one must recognize when the palace ruler generates or supports the degree ruler, or when the degree ruler generates or supports the palace ruler. In such cases, above and below interact, their *qi* harmonizes, and the outcome is often auspicious. Conversely, if the palace ruler exhausts or clashes with the degree ruler, or the degree ruler exhausts or clashes with the palace ruler, above and below fail to interact, their *qi* obstructed, and the outcome is often inauspicious.

Though this is an established method, exceptions exist: when strong, it is fitting to be restrained or drained; when weak, it is fitting to be generated or supported. This is the Dao of the sage in nurturing and assisting.

For external palaces such as wealth, property, and others, degree rulers also exist, all calculated from the life or body palace’s degree.
- If the life or body palace is in *Wu* (Horse) Palace at *Zhang* 10 degrees, the wealth palace is in *Si* (Snake) Palace.
- At *Zhen* 5 degrees, the siblings palace is in *Chen* (Dragon) Palace.
- At *Kang* 6 degrees, the property palace is in *Mao* (Rabbit) Palace.
- At *Xin* 4 degrees, the children palace is in *Yin* (Tiger) Palace.
- At *Ji* 9 degrees, the servants palace is in *Chou* (Ox) Palace.
- At *Niu* 4 degrees, the spouses palace is in *Zi* (Rat) Palace.
- At *Wei* 8 degrees, the illness palace is in *Hai* (Pig) Palace.
- At *Bi* 6 degrees, the migration palace is in *Xu* (Dog) Palace.
- At *Lou* 11 degrees, the official salary palace is in *You* (Rooster) Palace.
- At *Bi* 2 degrees, the fortune and virtue palace is in *Shen* (Monkey) Palace.
- At *Jing* 4 degrees, the appearance palace is in *Wei* (Sheep) Palace.
- From *Liu* initial degree onward, the pattern continues similarly.

Within the twelve palaces, there are instances where auspiciousness conceals inauspiciousness, or inauspiciousness conceals auspiciousness. For example, the sun, moon, metal, water, and purple *qi* are all auspicious deities, yet they may transform into adversities, punishments, imprisonment, *Yangren*, or *Qisha*—not necessarily auspicious. Fire, *Luo*, *Ji*, and *Bei* are all inauspicious malefics, yet they may transform into beneficence, emolument, nobility, literary brilliance, or fortune stars—not necessarily inauspicious.

When the hours of *Mao* (Rabbit), *Chen* (Dragon), *Si* (Snake), *Wu* (Horse), *Wei* (Sheep), or *Shen* (Monkey) govern, calculations for wealth, siblings, property, children, and servants should begin from the life palace’s degree. Those who calculate palaces without degrees err. When the hours of *You* (Rooster), *Xu* (Dog), *Hai* (Pig), *Zi* (Rat), *Chou* (Ox), or *Yin* (Tiger) govern, calculations for wealth, siblings, property, and other stars should begin from the body palace’s degree. Those who persist in starting from the life palace’s degree err further. These are unresolved doubts among the common folk; scholars should examine them carefully. The remainder is illustrated in the diagrams.

*Confucian School’s Reverence for Principle: A Balanced Study of Geomancy and Filial Piety, Scroll Four* concludes.

*Celestial Talisman Canon Preface*
*Confucian School’s Reverence for Principle: A Balanced Study of Geomancy and Filial Piety, Scroll Five*

Here begins this work with Rongcheng, appearing in the *Plain Book*, while Master Red Pine expounded it in the *Green Satchel Classic*, and Huang Shigong annotated it in the *Green Satchel Transmission*. By the Song dynasty, Master Chen Chuan further divided and explicated its sections, exhausting their subtleties. He elucidated the mechanisms of the fivefold connections and sixfold qi, revealing the secrets of generation, assistance, restraint, and drainage. Its principles are most comprehensive, its methods most refined. This is because the ancients followed the transformations of creation, and thus their applications achieved such marvels.

Yet these methods prove infallible only when qi and fortune are in ascendance, coinciding with true mountains and waters. The principles of *shu* and *ru* are as follows:

**Diagram of the Fivefold Movements**
This is the River Diagram’s fixed positions. Its celestial revolutions change yearly, with earth at the center to stabilize the four directions. Thus it is said: "The ruler governs while the rest each administer a direction, executing the ruler’s commands—hence, the ministers govern."

*Verse:*
Jia and Ji transform earth, Yi and Geng transform metal,
Bing and Xin bring forth water, raising sweet rains;
Fire emerges in the south, seeking Wu and Gui,
Ding and Ren transform wood, forming boundless forests.

**Diagram of the Sixfold Qi**
This is the Later Heaven’s flowing numbers. Its qi descends to earth, changing every sixty days. After Great Cold, *Jueyin*’s generative qi arises; after the Spring Equinox, *Shaoyin*’s expansive qi; after Grain Full, *Shaoyang*’s growing qi; after Great Heat, *Taiyin*’s central qi; after the Autumn Equinox, *Yangming*’s gathering qi; after Light Snow, *Taiyang*’s storing qi. Each node comprises three pentads, each pentad five days, further divided into seventy-two qi.

*Verse:*
The six qi are distinct, each spanning sixty days,
Great Cold’s wind and water trace their origins;
The sovereign and minister still precede damp earth,
Cold water ever yields to dry metal.

**Diagram of Ruling and Descending Qi**
This depicts yin and yang’s mutual revolutions, changing yearly. *Zi* and *Wu* oppose *Mao* and *You*; *Chou* and *Wei* oppose *Chen* and *Xu*; *Yin* and *Shen* oppose *Si* and *Hai*. Ruling and descending qi alternate in function, embodying yin and yang’s mutual concealment within their domains, while the five qi spread in sequence. All mechanisms of supplementation and drainage must be deduced from this.

*Verse:*
*Zi-Wu*’s sovereign fire and dry metal descend,
*Chou-Wei*’s damp earth and cold water unite,
*Yin-Shen*’s ministerial fire and wind-wood align,
The rest oppose likewise without exception.

**Diagram of Uneven Qi Transformations**
This illustrates qi transformations’ irregularity, changing yearly. There is excess, insufficiency, and balanced qi. Years like *Tianfu*, *Huitong*, *Tianfu Tong*, *Changsheng Tianfu*, and *Taiyi Tianfu* are all balanced-qi years. The rest exhibit excess or insufficiency, and the means of harmonizing them through restraint and transformation depend on the practitioner.

*Verse:*
*Taiyi Tianfu* is most auspicious,
At the *Changsheng* position, blessings know no bounds;
*Suihui* and *Tianfu* are both propitious,
*Tongfu* and *Tonghui* require careful deliberation.

**Diagram of Host Qi**
This depicts the five phases’ fixed positions, unchanging through the ages. Balanced qi brings fortune, while excess or insufficiency brings misfortune. To diminish excess and supplement insufficiency, harmonizing through restraint and transformation, again depends on the practitioner. Methods like the *Hongfan*’s five phases invert true principles, rendering fortune and misfortune unverifiable. Those who discern this and attain mastery will find their responses as swift as echo.

*Verse:*
Fiery flames blaze in the south, water resides in the north,
The east’s bending-straight and the west’s Venus stand;
*Xun* wood, *Qian* metal, *Kun* and *Gen* earth,
The Yellow Matriarch’s four tombs need no mention.

**Diagram of Guest Qi**
This depicts the five qi’s flow, changing with years and months. When balanced qi prevails, one must neither allow guest qi to generate nor drain. Only when host qi is excessive should guest qi be used to drain it; when host qi is insufficient, guest qi should be used to generate it. The initial qi is the host qi. While guest qi may bring fortune, it may also bring misfortune—one cannot adhere rigidly to a single principle.

*Verse:*
Water fears earth, wood fears metal,
The metal star dreads fire, fire dreads rain;
Even the Yellow Matriarch dislikes bending-straight,
Restraint and transformation demand careful application.

**Diagram of Generation, Assistance, Restraint, and Drainage**
The marvels of creation are perfected in harmony. Generation and assistance supplement insufficiency; restraint and drainage curb excess. Just as the reckless are restrained by sages, and the overcautious are urged forward, people know only to use generation and assistance, unaware of restraint and drainage. Yet both excess and insufficiency can bring disaster. This diagram is established for easy reference.

*Verse:*
The five qi’s uses originally differ,
Harmony alone achieves divine craft;
Excess demands restraint and drainage,
Insufficiency requires generation and assistance to succeed.

**The Fivefold Movements**
Jia and Ji transform earth, Yi and Geng transform metal,
Bing and Xin transform water, Ding and Ren transform wood,
Wu and Gui transform fire, with earth at the center to command the four directions.
Thus it is said: "The ruler governs while the rest each specialize in a direction to fulfill commands—hence, the ministers govern."

Master Chen Xiyi states: The fivefold movements are the ten celestial stems’ revolutions through heaven, changing yearly. Yang years’ fivefold movements manifest excessive qi; yin years’ fivefold movements manifest insufficient qi. Those without excess or insufficiency are balanced qi, assuredly bringing fortune. Those with excess or insufficiency are perverse qi, invariably bringing disaster.

Thus, in *Jia* years, earth qi is greatly excessive, yin qi prevails, and its perversity invades water. In *Yi* years, metal qi is insufficient, fiery qi prevails, and its perversity invades metal. In *Bing* years, water qi is greatly excessive, cold qi prevails, and its perversity invades fire. In *Ding* years, wood qi is insufficient, dry qi prevails, and its perversity invades wood. In *Wu* years, fire qi is greatly excessive, scorching heat prevails, and its perversity invades metal.

In *Ji* years, earth qi is insufficient, wind qi prevails, and its perversity invades earth. In *Geng* years, metal qi is greatly excessive, dry qi prevails, and its perversity invades wood. In *Xin* years, water qi is insufficient, damp qi prevails, and its perversity invades water. In *Ren* years, wood qi is greatly excessive, wind qi prevails, and its perversity invades earth. In *Gui* years, fire qi is insufficient, cold qi prevails, and its perversity invades fire.

Only in *Jia-chen*, *Shen-xu*, *Ji-chou*, and *Ji-wei* years is earth’s balanced qi present. In *Ren-yin*, *Ren-shen*, *Ding-mao*, *Ding-si*, and *Ding-hai* years, wood’s balanced qi is present. In *Wu-zi*, *Wu-wu*, *Wu-yin*, *Wu-shen*, *Gui-mao*, *Gui-si*, *Gui-you*, and *Gui-hai* years, water’s (Kan’s) balanced qi is present. In *Geng-zi*, *Geng-wu*, *Geng-shen*, *Yi-mao*, and *Yi-you* years, metal’s balanced qi is present. In *Bing-zi*, *Bing-chen*, *Bing-shen*, *Bing-xu*, *Xin-chou*, *Xin-mao*, *Xin-wei*, and *Xin-hai* years, water’s balanced qi is present.

This fool observes: *Yin* belongs to the tiger, *chen* to the dragon—nothing is as unpredictable in transformation as dragons and tigers. Thus, the qi of transformation takes the dragon and tiger months as its basis.

Therefore, in *Jia* and *Ji* years, the first month is established as *Bing-yin*; *Bing* fire must generate earth, and counting to the *chen* month, *Wu* appears—hence it is said: *Jia-Ji* transforms earth. In *Yi* and *Geng* years, the first month is established as *Wu-yin*; *Wu* earth must generate metal, and counting to the *chen* month, *Geng* appears—hence it is said: *Yi-Geng* transforms metal. In *Bing* and *Xin* years, the first month is established as *Geng-yin*; *Geng* metal must generate water, and counting to the *chen* month, *Ren* appears—hence it is said: *Bing-Xin* transforms water. In *Ding* and *Ren* years, the first month is established as *Ren-yin*; *Ren* water must generate wood, and counting to the *chen* month, *Jia* appears—hence it is said: *Ding-Ren* transforms wood. In *Wu* and *Gui* years, the first month is established as *Jia-yin*; *Jia* wood must generate fire, and counting to the *chen* month, *Bing* appears—hence it is said: *Wu-Gui* transforms fire.

Earth serves as the ruler’s governance, standing foremost among the fivefold connections. Earth generates metal, metal generates water, water generates wood, wood generates fire—following the cycle of generation, fire in turn generates earth; these are all the governance of ministers. Thus, they follow in sequence thereafter.

**The Six Qi**
From the beginning of Great Cold to the end of Awakening of Insects, *Jueyin* wind-wood governs, presiding over the qi of generation. From the beginning of Spring Equinox to the end of Summer Solstice, *Shaoyin* sovereign fire governs, presiding over the qi of expansion. From the beginning of Grain Full to the end of Slight Heat, *Shaoyang* ministerial fire governs, presiding over the qi of growth. From the beginning of Great Heat to the end of White Dew, *Taiyin* damp earth governs, presiding over the central qi. From the beginning of Autumn Equinox to the end of Beginning of Winter, *Yangming* dry metal governs, presiding over the qi of harvest. From the beginning of Slight Snow to the end of Slight Cold, *Taiyang* cold water governs, presiding over the qi of storage.

Master Chen of Xiyi says: The Six Qi are the qi of the twelve earthly branches, changing every sixty days. Each qi comprises four solar terms, each term three pentads, and each pentad five days.

Great Cold, Beginning of Spring, Rain Water, and Awakening of Insects are all times when wind-wood qi prevails—these forty-five days, its qi reaches due east. Spring Equinox, Pure Brightness, Grain Rain, and Beginning of Summer are all times when sovereign fire qi prevails; Grain Full, Grain in Ear, Summer Solstice, and Slight Heat are all times when ministerial fire qi prevails—these ninety days, its qi reaches due south. Great Heat, Beginning of Autumn, End of Heat, and White Dew are all times when damp earth qi prevails—these forty-five days, its qi reaches the four corners. Autumn Equinox, Cold Dew, Frost’s Descent, and Beginning of Winter are all times when dry metal qi prevails—these forty-five days, its qi reaches due west. Slight Snow, Great Snow, Winter Solstice, and Slight Cold are all times when cold water qi prevails—these forty-five days, its qi reaches due north.

Metal, water, earth, and wood all transform through form. Thus, when metal divides, it becomes light; when water divides, it becomes shallow; when earth divides, it becomes weak; when wood divides, it becomes small. Fire transforms through qi, becoming ever more abundant with division. Thus, metal, wood, water, and earth each have one, while fire alone has two.

This fool observes: To understand the movement of the Six Qi, one must also know the method of transition. Otherwise, one may err by acting before the qi arrives or after it has passed. Yet the Six Qi merely follow the seasons to determine their waxing and waning. In truth, only when qi and movement are united does supreme fortune arise.

**Heavenly Stems and Earthly Branches Governing Heaven and Earth**
In *Zi-Wu* years, sovereign fire governs heaven, dry metal resides in earth. In *Chou-Wei* years, damp earth governs heaven, cold water resides in earth. In *Yin-Shen* years, ministerial fire governs heaven, wind-wood resides in earth. In *Mao-You* years, dry metal governs heaven, sovereign fire resides in earth. In *Chen-Xu* years, cold water governs heaven, damp earth resides in earth. In *Si-Hai* years, wind-wood governs heaven, ministerial fire resides in earth.

Master Chen of Xiyi says: According to Jing Fang, *Taiyang* transforms into cold water, *Yangming* into dry metal, *Shaoyang* into ministerial fire, *Taiyin* into damp earth, and *Jueyin* into wind-wood. Thus, in *Zi-Wu* years, *Shaoyin* governs heaven, *Yangming* resides in earth. In *Chou-Wei* years, *Taiyin* governs heaven, *Taiyang* resides in earth. In *Yin-Shen* years, *Shaoyang* governs heaven, *Jueyin* resides in earth. In *Mao-You* years, *Yangming* governs heaven, *Shaoyin* resides in earth. In *Chen-Xu* years, *Taiyang* governs heaven, *Taiyin* resides in earth. In *Si-Hai* years, *Jueyin* governs heaven, *Shaoyang* resides in earth.

This fool observes: In *Zi-Wu* years, sovereign fire governs heaven, for fire can generate earth.

Thus, in *Chou-Wei* years, damp earth follows, for sovereign fire is too weak to govern alone. In *Yin-Shen* years, ministerial fire follows, as earth flourishes to generate metal. In *Mao-You* years, dry metal follows, as metal flourishes to generate water. In *Chen-Xu* years, cold water follows, as water flourishes to generate wood. In *Si-Hai* years, wind-wood follows. This is the sequence of the celestial governors, completing a cycle of generation, where wood in turn generates fire.

In *Zi-Wu* years, dry metal resides in earth, and as metal flourishes, it generates water. Thus, in *Chou-Wei* years, cold water follows, and as water flourishes, it generates wood. In *Yin-Shen* years, wind-wood follows, and as wood flourishes, it generates fire. In *Mao-You* years, sovereign fire follows, for fire can generate earth. In *Chen-Xu* years, damp earth follows, but as sovereign fire is still weak, ministerial fire succeeds it. This is the sequence of the terrestrial governors, completing a cycle of generation, where earth in turn generates metal and stone.

Is this not the Dao of the ceaseless generation of the Five Phases? Moreover, *Zi-Wu* and *Mao-You* stand in opposition, *Chou-Wei* and *Chen-Xu* stand in opposition, and *Yin-Shen* and *Si-Hai* stand in opposition—is this not the Dao of the Five Phases mutually concealing their abodes?

**Host Qi and Guest Qi**
When the first qi of water encounters earth, metal, water, and fire all become guest qi. When the first qi of fire encounters earth, metal, water, and wood all become guest qi. When the second qi encounters metal, water, wood, and fire all become guest qi. When the first qi of metal encounters water, wood, fire, and earth all become guest qi. When the first qi of water encounters wood, fire, earth, and metal all become guest qi.

Master Chen of Xiyi says: Dragons arriving from the east are governed by the qi of wind-wood; those from the south by the qi of sovereign and ministerial fire; those from the four corners by the qi of damp earth; those from the west by the qi of dry metal; and those from the north by the qi of cold water. All qi beyond the host qi are guest qi.

This fool observes: The east as wood, the south as fire, the west as metal, the north as water, and the four corners as earth—these are the host qi, enduring unchanged through all ages. Guest qi, however, shift with each year and month, ceaselessly altering without constraint, as seen in the varying celestial governors and terrestrial residences each year, and the cyclical succession of spring, summer, autumn, and winter. When guest qi bring fortune, all is auspicious; when they bring misfortune, all is inauspicious. If the host qi is strong, that which restrains me is auspicious, while that which generates me is inauspicious. If the host qi is weak, that which generates me is auspicious, while that which restrains me is inauspicious. For the host qi is still, while the guest qi are dynamic. As the *Yi Jing* states: "Good and ill fortune, regret and remorse, arise from movement."

**Heavenly Convergence (Tianfu)**
*Wu-yin*, *Wu-shen*, *Wu-zi*, *Wu-wu*, *Bing-chen*, *Bing-xu*, *Ding-si*, *Ding-hai*, *Ji-chou*, *Ji-wei*, *Yi-mao*, *Yi-you*—in these, the qi of transformation aligns with the celestial governor, hence they are called *Tianfu*.

**Yearly Convergence (Suihui Tianfu)**
*Jia-chen*, *Jia-xu*, *Ji-chou*, *Ji-wei*, *Yi-you*, *Geng-shen*, *Bing-zi*, *Xin-hai*, *Ren-yin*, *Ding-mao*, *Wu-wu*, *Gui-si*—in these, the qi of transformation aligns with the year’s cyclical sign, hence they are called *Suihui Tianfu*.

**Convergence with Heaven (Tongtianfu)**
*Jia-chen*, *Jia-xu*, *Geng-zi*, *Geng-wu*, *Ren-yin*, *Ren-shen*—in these, the yang-year’s qi of transformation aligns with the terrestrial residence, hence they are called *Tongtianfu*.

**Convergence with the Year (Tongsuihui Tianfu)**
*Xin-chou*, *Xin-wei*, *Gui-si*, *Gui-hai*, *Gui-mao*, *Gui-you*—in these, the yin-year’s qi of transformation aligns with the terrestrial residence, hence they are called *Tongsuihui Tianfu*.

**Grand Unity Heavenly Convergence (Taiyi Tianfu)**
*Ji-wei*, *Ji-chou*, *Yi-you*, *Wu-wu*—these are both *Tianfu* and *Suihui*, hence they are called *Taiyi Tianfu*.

**Vital Birth Heavenly Convergence (Changsheng Tianfu)**
*Wu-yin*, *Gui-you*, *Bing-shen*, *Xin-mao*—in these, the qi of transformation occupies the position of vital birth, hence they are called *Changsheng Tianfu*. Though *Jia-yin* occupies the position of vital birth, earth qi is restrained and thus not employed. Though *Ji-you* occupies the position of vital birth, the *xiaoshen* (ominous spirit) coincides with generation and thus is not employed. Though *Wu-yin* encounters the *xiaoshen*, it also aligns with *Tianfu* and may be used.

**The Sixty Characters of Heavenly Convergence**
*Ding-mao*, *Geng-wu*, *Xin-wei*, *Ren-shen*, *Gui-you*, *Jia-xu*, *Bing-zi*, *Wu-yin*, *Yi-you*, *Bing-xu*, *Ding-hai*, *Wu-zi*, *Ji-chou*, *Xin-mao*, *Gui-si*, *Bing-shen*, *Geng-zi*, *Xin-chou*, *Ren-yin*, *Gui-mao*, *Jia-chen*, *Wu-shen*, *Xin-hai*, *Yi-mao*, *Bing-chen*, *Ding-si*, *Wu-wu*, *Ji-wei*, *Geng-shen*, *Gui-hai*.

This fool observes: The sixty characters of *Tianfu* are derived from the pairing of the Five Movements with the Six Qi, akin to the *Dayan* number. Fifty is obtained by multiplying the central heaven-five of the *Hetu* by the earth-ten. Now, if these sixty characters are each expanded to form configurations of their original qi, they become minor hexagrams. If these sixty characters are fully expanded to form configurations of mixed qi, they become major hexagrams. Further extended and elaborated upon, they multiply endlessly—is this not comparable to the *Dayan* hexagrams, which number four thousand ninety-six?

**Transcending Spirit and Connecting Qi**
A solar term is divided into three pentads, each pentad spanning five days. For instance, *Jia-zi*, *Jia-wu*, *Ji-mao*, and *Ji-you* mark the first pentad; *Jia-yin*, *Jia-shen*, *Ji-si*, and *Ji-hai* mark the middle pentad; and *Jia-chen*, *Jia-xu*, *Ji-chou*, and *Ji-wei* mark the final pentad. If the transition of a solar term occurs later while the first pentad’s marker appears earlier, the spirit is transcended and the marker is employed. If the transition occurs earlier while the first pentad’s marker appears later, the qi must be connected, and the term is not employed. Such is the method of transcending spirit and connecting qi.

I observe: when *qi* precedes the solar term, it is called *spirit*; when *spirit* follows the solar term, it is called *qi*—*spirit* and *qi* are one and the same, differing only in name. For example, if the first pentad’s marker appears three days before *Lichun* (Beginning of Spring), it is employed as the *Lichun* solar term—this is what is meant by *transcending spirit*. If the first pentad’s marker appears three days after *Lichun*, one must wait until the marker’s day to employ *Lichun* as the solar term—this is what is meant by *connecting qi*. Whether the discrepancy is one or two days, or four, five, or six days, the principle remains the same. If the first pentad’s marker arrives on the same day, that day is used as the starting time; the same applies to *transcending* and *connecting* above. Five time-periods make one pentad, and three pentads comprise fifteen time-periods.

**Celestial Correspondences: A Query**
Some may ask: the method of *Celestial Correspondences* is based on balanced *qi*. Whether in excess or deficiency, it can bring about calamity. This is the true orthodoxy of the art of selection, unchanging even after ten thousand generations. Yet, upon examining its application, doubts may arise. For instance, in yin-years, when *qi* is deficient, it should be supplemented. Thus, in all *yi*-years, metal is deficient, but in *yi-mao* and *yi-you*, the metal of the *Controlling Heaven* supplements it, and in *yi-you*, the *Yearly Assembly* further supplements it. In all *ding*-years, wood is deficient, but in *ding-hai* and *ding-si*, the wood of the *Controlling Heaven* supplements it, and in *ding-mao*, the *Yearly Assembly* supplements it. In all *ji*-years, earth is deficient, but in *ji-chou* and *ji-wei*, the earth of the *Controlling Heaven* supplements it, and the *Yearly Assembly* further supplements it. In all *xin*-years, water is deficient, but in *xin-chou* and *xin-wei*, the water of the *Subterranean Spring* supplements it, and in *xin-hai*, the *Yearly Assembly* supplements it. In all *gui*-years, fire is deficient, but in *gui-mao*, *gui-si*, *gui-you*, and *gui-hai*, the fire of the *Subterranean Spring* supplements it.

Yet, in all *jia*-years, earth is in excess, so why do *jia-chen* and *jia-xu* have the earth of the *Yearly Assembly* to supplement it? In all *bing*-years, water is in excess, so why do *bing-chen* and *bing-xu* have the water of the *Controlling Heaven* to supplement it, and *bing-shen* the water of *Long Life* to supplement it? In all *wu*-years, fire is in excess, so why do *wu-zi*, *wu-yin*, *wu-wu*, and *wu-shen* have the fire of the *Controlling Heaven* to supplement it, and *wu-wu* the fire of *Taiyi* to supplement it? In all *geng*-years, metal is in excess, so why do *geng-zi* and *geng-wu* have the metal of the *Same Celestial Correspondence* to supplement it? In all *ren*-years, wood is in excess, so why do *ren-yin* and *ren-shen* have the wood of the *Subterranean Spring* to supplement it, and *ren-yin* the *Yearly Assembly* to supplement it?

To these doubts, the answer is: excess must reach its extreme before it can return to the mean. Just as cold must reach its utmost before warmth arises, and heat must peak before coolness emerges. The *Yijing* states: "When the sun reaches its zenith, it declines; when the moon is full, it wanes." Master Shao likewise regarded the full bloom of flowers as the onset of decay, and the moment of fragrant blossoming as the peak of vitality—all reflecting this principle. Only in the five yin-years, like a person of insufficient strength, must one be aided and supported before success can be achieved. Reflect upon this, and the reasoning will become clear.

**The Above Passage**
This chapter consists entirely of ancient sayings, annotated and expounded by Master Chen Xiyi.

**Elaboration on Celestial Correspondences**
*Correspondence* means alignment; *constant* means regularity. It signifies that when aligned with the celestial *qi* and its movements, it becomes the most correct and enduring Dao. Thus, it is said: the *Celestial Correspondences* are the true canon. I once reverently studied the Yellow Emperor, who commanded *Darao* to observe the handle of the Dipper and create the *jiazi* system, and *Rongcheng* to synthesize the six arts and determine the *qi* and its movements—this marked the beginning of *Celestial Correspondences*. Later, *Gui Yuqu* mastered it and composed the *Divine Calendar*, while *Qibo* transmitted the *Inner Canon*. Yao’s "revering the vast heavens and respectfully receiving the seasons," Shun’s alignment of the seven celestial bodies with the *jiheng*, and the calendrical and temporal governance of Yu, Tang, Wen, and Wu—all followed this Dao. Alas, after the Qin’s burning of books, these methods were lost. Only Master Chen Xiyi, in his later work, uniquely grasped its profound subtleties with his own insight, aligning with the unbroken lineage of the ancient emperors. The five movements and six *qi* have fixed principles; the *Controlling Heaven* and *Subterranean Spring* have definitive judgments. All mechanisms of host and guest, victory and defeat, are thoroughly illuminated in their secrets.

Yet, though the ancient kings revealed its essence, later practitioners have since corrupted it. Thus, for hundreds of years until now, no one has truly understood its core. They merely know the time when the *qi* of the year arrives, claiming it sufficient for siting graves and dwellings, while disregarding whether the year, month, day, and hour align. Is this not why fortune and misfortune remain unpredictable?

After deep and repeated contemplation, I have finally grasped its teachings. Within it, there are *Celestial Correspondences*, *Yearly Assembly Celestial Correspondences*, *Same Celestial Correspondences*, *Same Yearly Assembly Celestial Correspondences*, as well as *Taiyi Celestial Correspondences* and *Long Life Celestial Correspondences*. Though the words are concise, they encompass vast meaning; though the intent is simple, it is exceedingly detailed. Yet, practitioners fail to understand it, and scholars have no time to study it—thus, the profound learning of the ancients has long remained obscure to later generations. I have therefore fully elaborated its principles to share with the world. This method neither avoids inauspicious spirits nor requires auspicious omens.

Only when the year, month, day, and hour all align with the *Celestial Correspondences* should one act—when in ascendance, it is fitting to restrain or drain; when in decline, it is fitting to nurture or support. The configuration must attain harmony before application. In great matters, this can be used to establish states and found nations; in small matters, to secure graves and settle dwellings. Even without aligning with the seven luminaries of the astral chart, one may still achieve the method of auspicious selection. This is the most correct and essential principle, which I have elaborated into fixed configurations below. If further aligned with an auspicious astral chart, the blessings will be even greater.

This section specifically discusses the *Dragon*, unrelated to sitting orientation.

**Eastern Dragon**
This is the direction governed by the qi of Wind and Wood.

*Pure Qi Celestial Correspondences*
Suitable for: *renyin*, *renshen*, *dingmao*, *dingsi*, *dinghai*.
Year, month, day, and hour must all align.

*Mixed Qi Celestial Correspondences*
For year and day: *renyin*, *renshen*, *dingmao*, *dingsi*, *dinghai*, *bingchen*, *bingxu*, *bingzi*, *bingshen*, *xinchou*, *xinmao*, *xinwei*, *xinhai*, as well as *jiachen*, *jiaxu*, *jichou*, *jiwei*.
For month and hour: *renyin*, *jiachen*, *xinhai*, *xinmao*, *xinchou*, *bingshen*, *dingmao*, *xinwei*, *renshen*, *jiaxu*, *bingzi*, as well as *xinchou* and *jichou* hours.
All above are cases where Wind-Wood qi attains balance.
Excluded are: *renzhi*, *renchen*, *renwu*, *renxu*, *bingyin*, *bingwu*, *jiazi*, *jiachen*, *jiawu*, *jiashen* (all cases of excessive transformation), and *dingchou*, *dingwei*, *dingyou*, *xinsi*, *xinyou*, *xinmao*, *jimao*, *jisi*, *jiyou*, *jihai* (all cases of insufficient transformation).

**Southern Dragon**
This is the direction governed by the qi of Sovereign and Ministerial Fire.

*Pure Qi Celestial Correspondences*
Suitable for: *wuzi*, *wuwu*, *wuyin*, *wushen*, *guimao*, *guiyou*, *guisi*, *guihai*.
Year, month, day, and hour must all align.

*Mixed Qi Celestial Correspondences*
For year and day: *wuzi*, *wuwu*, *wuyin*, *wushen*, *guimao*, *guiyou*, *guisi*, *guihai*, *renyin*, *renshen*, *dingmao*, *dingsi*, *dinghai*, as well as *gengzi*, *gengwu*, *gengshen*, *jimao*, *you*.
For month and hour: *yimao*, *dingsi*, *wuwu*, *gengjia*, *guihai*, *renyin*, *guimao*, *wushen*, *wuyin*, *you*, *dinghai*, *wuzi*, as well as *gengzi* hour.
All above are cases where Sovereign and Ministerial Fire qi attains balance.
Excluded are: *wuchen*, *wuxu*, *renzi*, *renchen*, *renwu*, *gengyin*, *gengchen*, *gengxu* (all cases of excessive transformation), and *guichou*, *guiwei*, *dingwei*, *dingyou*, *dingchou*, *yisi*, *yiwei*, *yihai* (all cases of insufficient transformation).

**Four-Corner Dragons**
This is the direction governed by the qi of Damp Earth.

*Pure Qi Celestial Correspondences*
Suitable for: *jiachen*, *jiaxu*, *jichou*, *jiwei*.
Year, month, day, and hour must all align.

*Mixed Qi Celestial Correspondences*
For year and day: *jiachen*, *jiaxu*, *jichou*, *jiwei*, *wuyin*, *wuwu*, *wuzi*, *wushen*, *guimao*, *guiyou*, *guisi*, *guihai*, as well as *bingzi*, *bingshen*, *bingchen*, *bingxu*, *xinchou*, *xinwei*, *xinmao*, *xinhai*.
For month and hour: *xinwei*, *guiyou*, *jiaxu*, *bingzi*, *bingchen*, *wuwu*, *jiwei*, *guihai*, *xinmao*, *guisi*, *bingshen*, *xinchou*, as well as *wuzi* hour.
All above are cases where Damp Earth qi attains balance.
Excluded are: *jiazi*, *jiachen*, *jiawu*, *jiashen*, *wuchen*, *wuxu*, *bingyin*, *bingwu* (all cases of excessive transformation), and *jimao*, *jisi*, *jiyou*, *jihai*, *guiwei*, *guichou*, *xinsi*, *xinyou* (all cases of insufficient transformation).

**Western Dragon**
This is the direction governed by the qi of Dry Metal.

*Pure Qi Celestial Correspondences*
Suitable for: *gengzi*, *gengwu*, *gengshen*, *yimao*, *you*.
Year, month, day, and hour must all align.

*Mixed Qi Celestial Correspondences*
For year and day: *gengshen*, *gengwu*, *gengzi*, *yimao*, *you*, *jiachen*, *jiaxu*, *jichou*, *jiwei*, as well as *renyin*, *renshen*, *dingmao*, *dinghai*, *dingsi*.
For month and hour: *you*, *dinghai*, *jichou*, *dingmao*, *gengwu*, *renshen*, *jiaxu*, *renyin*, *jiachen*, as well as *gengzi* hour.
Excluded are: *gengchen*, *gengxu*, *gengyin*, *jiazi*, *jiachen*, *jiawu*, *jiashen*, *renchen*, *renwu*, *renxu*, *renzi* (all cases of excessive transformation), and *yichou*, *yisi*, *yiwei*, *yihai*, *yimao*, *jisi*, *jihai*, *dingchou*, *dingwei*, *dingyou* (all cases of insufficient transformation).

**Northern Dragon**
This is the direction governed by the qi of Cold Water.

*Pure Qi Celestial Correspondences*
Suitable for: *bingzi*, *bingchen*, *bingshen*, *bingxu*, *xinchou*, *xinmao*, *xinwei*, *xinhai*.
Year, month, day, and hour must all align.

*Mixed Qi Celestial Correspondences*
