For year and day: *bingzi*, *bingchen*, *bingshen*, *bingxu*, *xinmao*, *xinwei*, *xinhai*, *xinchou*, *gengzi*, *gengwu*, *gengshen*, *yimao*, *you*, as well as *wuzi*, *wuyin*, *wuwu*, *wushen*, *guimao*, *guisi*, *guiyou*, *guihai*.
For month and hour: *xinmao*, *guisi*, *bingshen*, *gengzi*, *xinchou*, *wuyin*, *you*, *bingxu*, *wuzi*, *yimao*, *bingchen*, *wuwu*, *gengshen*, *guihai*, as well as *wuzi* and *bingzi* hours.
All above are cases where Cold Water qi attains balance.

**Excess and Deficiency in Transformation Qi**

*Excessive Transformation Qi*
*Bingyin*, *bingwu*, *wuchen*, *wuxu*, *gengyin*, *gengchen*, *gengxu* all manifest excessive transformation qi.

*Deficient Transformation Qi*
*Xinsi*, *xinyou*, *guichou*, *guiwei*, *yisi*, *yiwei*, *yihai*, *yichou* all manifest deficient transformation qi.

The above four pillars employ only their native qi without admixture, termed *Zhengqi Tianfu* (Pure Qi Celestial Correspondences). When the four pillars employ either native qi, generative qi, or wealth qi in mixed combination, this is termed *Zaqi Tianfu* (Mixed Qi Celestial Correspondences). Though their names differ, their auspicious effects are the same.

If the selection aligns with year, month, day, and hour, it is most auspicious—even without matching the Seven Governors’ stellar configuration, it may still confer blessings. Only avoid sitting with the Three Killings in dominance or facing the Grand Year Star in dominance; other inauspicious spirits and baleful stars need not be feared.

Should the Seven Governors’ stellar configuration also align, this becomes a once-in-ten-thousand selection, most auspicious indeed. For those beyond the circle of balance—where excess prevails—reduce the excess to attain moderation; where deficiency prevails, draw forth the deficiency to reach equilibrium. Thus, through regulation and transformation, one achieves harmony indistinguishable from balanced qi. If the Seven Governors’ configuration also proves flawless, the arrangement is complete. Yet one must not be rigidly bound by the Seven Governors.

When Dragon qi is vigorous, even if the pillars employ restraining or draining qi, no harm arises. When Dragon qi is weak, only generative reinforcement brings auspiciousness. These two principles depend on human adaptation.

*Zhengqi Tianfu* and *Zaqi Tianfu* may be employed even by beginners. However, the *Tianfu* standard configuration may occasionally appear in discourse. Beyond this, there are *Huaxiang* (Transformation Resemblance) configurations, *Leixiang* (Category Resemblance) configurations, and six auspicious *Ge* (Format) configurations, all resembling the *Tianfu* standard. It suffices to ensure the Sun arrives at the sitting or facing direction, or the Emperor Star arrives at the sitting direction, while avoiding the Three Killings and not facing the Grand Year Star—all such periods may be used.

The methods for these three configurations are illustrated below. Not all need align perfectly; any may be employed.

**1. Huaxiang Configuration**
This configuration requires the Heavenly Stems to undergo dual transformation while the Earthly Branches form a triple union.

**2. Leixiang Configuration**
This configuration requires each element to follow its category—Wood for Wood, Fire for Fire—while the Earthly Branches form a triple union. The rest follow accordingly.

**3. Six Ge Configurations**
This configuration requires adherence to standard formats:
- For *guan* (official) or *sha* (punishment) with weak vitality, use generative qi;
- For *yin* (seal) with strong vitality, use wealth qi;
- For light *yin*, favor *guan*;
- For heavy *yin*, favor wealth;
- For abundant wealth, favor *guan* or *sha*;
- For weak wealth, fear plunder;
- *Shishen* (Food Spirit) prefers singularity; three become *shang* (injury).
- For *shangguan* (Injury Officer) with strong vitality, favor wealth or *sha*; with weak vitality, favor *yin* (seal), though wealth and *yin* must not both flourish.
*Master Zi Ping* often said: If *shangguan*, wealth, and *yin* all flourish, whence comes fortune?

**Dragon Configurations**
Wind-Wood Dragon, Fire-Fire Dragon, Damp-Earth Dragon, Dry-Metal Dragon, Cold-Water Dragon—all are assessed vertically and horizontally.

**Transformation of Heavenly Stems and Earthly Branches**
- *Jia* and *Ji* transform in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Yi* and *Geng* transform in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Bing* and *Xin* transform in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Ding* and *Ren* transform in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Wu* and *Gui* transform in years, months, days, and hours.

**Earthly Branches Aligning with Elemental Configurations**
- Earthly Branches in Earth configuration;
- Earthly Branches in Metal configuration;
- Earthly Branches in Water configuration;
- Earthly Branches in Wood configuration (or Water, Earth, Metal, or Wood);
- Earthly Branches in Fire configuration (or Water, Earth, Metal, or Wood).

**Wealth Qi Configuration**
When dominant, auspicious; when weak, inauspicious.
- *Yi* and *Geng* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Bing* and *Xin* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Ding* and *Ren* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Wu* and *Gui* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Jia* and *Ji* in years, months, days, and hours.

Earthly Branches in Metal, Water, Wood, Fire, or Earth configurations (or Earth, Metal, Water, Wood, or Fire).

**Restraining Qi Configuration**
When dominant, no harm; when weak, extremely inauspicious.
- *Bing* and *Xin* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Ding* and *Ren* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Wu* and *Gui* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Jia* and *Ji* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Yi* and *Geng* in years, months, days, and hours.

Earthly Branches in Water, Wood, Fire, Earth, or Metal configurations (or Wood, Fire, Earth, Metal, or Water).

**Generative Qi Configuration**
When dominant, moderately auspicious; when weak, extremely auspicious.
- *Ding* and *Ren* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Wu* and *Gui* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Jia* and *Ji* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Yi* and *Geng* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Bing* and *Xin* in years, months, days, and hours.

Earthly Branches in Wood, Fire, Earth, Metal, or Water configurations (or Water, Wood, Fire, Earth, or Metal).

**Native Qi Configuration**
Perfect harmony is most auspicious; excess or deficiency is inauspicious.
- *Wu* and *Gui* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Jia* and *Ji* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Yi* and *Geng* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Bing* and *Xin* in years, months, days, and hours;
- *Ding* and *Ren* in years, months, days, and hours.

Earthly Branches in Fire, Earth, Metal, Water, or Wood configurations (or Metal, Water, Wood, Fire, or Earth).

**Draining Qi Configuration**
When weak, extremely inauspicious; when dominant, no harm.

**Dragon Directions**
Eastern Dragon, Southern Dragon, Four-Corner Dragons, Western Dragon, Northern Dragon.

**Horizontal and Vertical Analysis of Configurations**

**Generative Qi Configuration**
When weak, most auspicious; when dominant, inauspicious.

**Yang Stems**
Yang Wood: *Jia* day; Yang Fire: *Bing* day; Yang Earth: *Wu* day; Yang Metal: *Geng* day; Yang Water: *Ren* day.
- *Jia, Bing, Wu, Geng, Ren*: Peer support.
  When weak, auspicious; when wealthy, auspicious; when dominant, loss of wealth.
- *Yi, Ding, Ji, Xin, Gui*: Rob Wealth.
  When wealthy and weak, auspicious; when dominant and wealth is light, inauspicious.
- *Bing, Wu, Geng, Ren, Jia*: Food Spirit.
  When dominant, wealth is suitable; when weak, seal is suitable; otherwise, inauspicious.
- *Ding, Ji, Xin, Gui, Yi*: Hurting Officer.
  When dominant, wealth is suitable; when weak, seal is suitable; otherwise, inauspicious.
- *Wu, Geng, Ren, Jia, Bing*: Indirect Wealth.
  Officials and killers are suitable; when dominant, auspicious; when weak, inauspicious.
- *Ji, Xin, Gui, Yi, Ding*: Direct Wealth.
  Same as above.
- *Geng, Ren, Jia, Bing, Wu*: Indirect Officer.
  When dominant, wealth is suitable; when weak, Seven Killings and seal are suitable; all favor dominance.
- *Xin, Gui, Yi, Ding, Ji*: Direct Officer.
  Same as above.
- *Ren, Jia, Bing, Wu, Geng*: Indirect Seal.
  When dominant, inauspicious; when weak, also auspicious.
- *Gui, Yi, Ding, Ji, Xin*: Direct Seal.
  Also known as Owl Spirit; same as above.

**Yin Stems**
Yin Wood: *Yi* day; Yin Fire: *Ding* day; Yin Earth: *Ji* day; Yin Metal: *Xin* day; Yin Water: *Gui* day.
- *Jia, Bing, Wu, Geng, Ren*: Rob Wealth.
  When wealthy and weak, auspicious; when dominant and wealth is light, inauspicious.
- *Yi, Ding, Ji, Xin, Gui*: Peer support.
  Same as above.
- *Bing, Wu, Geng, Ren, Jia*: Hurting Officer.
  When dominant, wealth is suitable; when weak, seal is suitable; otherwise, inauspicious.
- *Ding, Ji, Xin, Gui, Yi*: Food Spirit.
  Same as above.
- *Wu, Geng, Ren, Jia, Bing*: Direct Wealth.
  Officials and killers are suitable; when dominant, auspicious; when weak, inauspicious.
- *Ji, Xin, Gui, Yi, Ding*: Indirect Wealth.
  Same as above.
- *Geng, Ren, Jia, Bing, Wu*: Direct Officer.
  When weak, seal is suitable; when dominant, wealth is suitable; favor dominance and use.
- *Xin, Gui, Yi, Ding, Ji*: Indirect Officer.
  Also known as Seven Killings; same as above.
- *Ren, Jia, Bing, Wu, Geng*: Direct Seal.
  When weak, auspicious; when dominant, inauspicious.
- *Gui, Yi, Ding, Ji, Xin*: Indirect Seal.
  Also known as Owl Spirit; same as above.

The above three configurations are residual methods of Heavenly Correspondence, all applied in the study of Dragons. For the auspiciousness or inauspiciousness of sitting and facing directions, refer to the preceding sections.

*Record of Fulfilling Filial Piety in Geomancy, Compiled by a Confucian Scholar Advocating Principle and Moderation, Volume Five—Concluded.*

**#1** *"Xū"* was originally miswritten as *"chéng"*—corrected based on context.
**#2** *"Hé"* was originally miswritten as *"hé"*—corrected based on context.
**#3** **#4** *"Lèi"* was originally written as *"chàn"*—suspected error, amended per context.

*Record of Fulfilling Filial Piety in Geomancy, Compiled by a Confucian Scholar Advocating Principle and Moderation, Volume Six*
*Excerpts from* **The Nine Palaces and Purple-White** *by Xu of Qiantang*

Xu of Qiantang, a scholar of profound learning, often delved into the abstruse mysteries of the Dao amid his studies of the Classics and histories. He extensively explored the principles of yin-yang creation, the waxing and waning of cosmic forces, and the profound workings of transformation. Having directly perceived the true mechanism, he composed *The Nine Palaces and Purple-White*, a discourse that particularly expounds what former sages had left unspoken—indeed, a work that complements the *Heavenly Correspondence Classic*. Here, I compile its essence for those who savor such wisdom to ponder together.

### **General Discussion on the Waxing and Waning of the Nine Palaces and Purple-White**

The pairing of purple and white with the Nine Palaces represents the fundamental nature of the initially divided directions. The interweaving of the Nine Palaces with the Eight Trigrams embodies the profound mechanism of the Later Heaven sequence in practical application.

With forty-five, it governs the framework of the eight solar terms;
With fifteen, it distributes the circulation of a single *qi*.
North belongs to *Kan*, south to *Li*, east to *Zhen*, and west to *Dui*—establishing the four cardinal positions.
The merits and faults of the central *qi*’s duration determine the four corners: spring to *Gen*, autumn to *Kun*, summer to *Xun*, and winter to *Qian*—dividing the four intercardinal sectors.
The alternations of cold and warmth in the solar terms are further refined into seventy-two migratory phases, advancing and retreating through three hundred and sixty cycles of waxing and waning. When yin and yang intermingle, their full potential is employed; when they stand alone, half is utilized.

Yet why are they matched with distinct stars such as *Greedy Wolf*, *Great Gate*, and *Military Arts*, while the original stars of the Nine Palaces are disregarded? Why are the transformed trigrams of *Generative Qi*, *Heavenly Physician*, and *Fortune-Virtue* emphasized, while the original trigrams of the eight directions are undervalued? Thus, without discerning host and guest, flying and hidden, waxing and waning, or the interactions of restraint, depletion, transformation, and harmony, some arbitrarily deem purple and white auspicious—I fail to comprehend this.

For instance:
- *One White*, belonging to water, becomes a killer when applied to *Fire-Mountain*;
- *Six White*, belonging to metal, becomes a killer when applied to *Wood-Mountain*;
- *Eight White*, belonging to earth, becomes a killer when applied to *Water-Mountain*;
- *Nine Purple*, belonging to fire, becomes a killer when applied to *Metal-Mountain*.

Moreover, the severity varies with strength and weakness: a mild killer acts as an official, while a severe one becomes a ghost; a strong self is beneficial, while a weak one invites disaster. Even if *Morning Audience* brings fortune, a shallow root and feeble power may not confer true favor. Though *Leakage* drains *qi*, a child rescuing its mother ultimately averts great misfortune. How can purple and white be deemed entirely auspicious, while other stars are wholly inauspicious?

Those so-called *Celestial Aperture*, *White Heavenly Mirror*, *Mystery Mechanism*, *Celestial Fortune*, and other charts are nothing but deceptions that delude the world and mislead the people. They invent elaborate names to astonish the senses: when speaking of fortune, they invoke *Celestial Emolument*, *Celestial Fortune*, *Celestial Virtue*, *Celestial Wealth*, and the like, inciting insatiable desires; when speaking of misfortune, they invoke *Celestial Lament*, *Celestial Resentment*, *Celestial Disaster*, *Celestial Calamity*, and the like, instilling fear and unease. Yet when questioned on the Five Phases, mutual generation and restraint, yin-yang, or waxing and waning, they offer nothing but empty words. Is the principle of the *Luo River Diagram* unreliable? Does the form of purple and white follow some other doctrine?

Where there is substance, there is form—the colors of the Nine Palaces arise therefrom.
Where there is form, there is nature—the principles of the nine colors are thus determined.
Where there are directions, there are superimpositions—the ceaseless cycle of day and night.
Where there are superimpositions, there are sequences and reversals—the alternating dominance of winter and summer.
Where there are heaven and earth, there is interdependence—the three epochs each govern their respective phases.
Where there are cyclical *qi*, there are returns—the six *jia* periodically revert to their origins.

Thus, Chen Tuan elucidated the diagram: at the winter solstice, *jia-zi* begins at *Kan*, proceeding sequentially through the Nine Palaces to observe the growth of yang *qi*; at the summer solstice, *jia-zi* begins at *Li*, flying in reverse through the nine colors to perceive the inception of yin *qi*. The waxing and waning of yin and yang are verifiable, and the generation and restraint of the Five Phases are precise. To abandon what has already been expounded and boast of what has not been transmitted is like a painter who, finding it difficult to deceive others with familiar subjects, resorts to depicting ghosts and demons to stir the imagination.

I shall take the *Luo River Diagram* and elucidate the principles of the Nine Palaces and Eight Trigrams, revealing the mechanisms of generation, restraint, waxing, and waning. Will this not immediately expose their fallacies and deceptions?

Alas! Our dynasty selects scholars through the examination system, leaving them no leisure to attend to such arts—hence these doctrines proliferate in confusion. If one were to calmly observe the forms of the four cardinal and five intercardinal directions, harmonizing their natures of metal, wood, water, and fire; dynamically examine the origins of their flow and concealment, weighing their applications of advance, retreat, augmentation, and reduction—then the ascent and descent of heaven and earth, the contraction and extension of ghosts and spirits, could not escape the bounds of this diagram.

Accordingly, I arrange its essentials below:

**One White** resides in *Kan*, its movement belongs to water. *Yang* water.
Born in *shen*, declines in *you*, flourishes in *zi* (midwinter), is entombed in *chen*, and perishes in *xun-si*.
Encountering metal becomes *seal*; earth, *killer*; wood, *depletion*; fire, *wealth*; water, *companion*.
In winter, it is the ruling star; in spring, it rests; in summer, it is imprisoned; in autumn, it is ministerial; in the four transitional seasons, it is restrained.
In years, months, days, or hours of metal or water, it is imbued with *qi*—auspicious when waxing or flourishing, inauspicious when entombed or perishing.

**Two Black** resides in *Kun*, its movement belongs to earth. *Yin* earth.
Born in *shen*, declines in *you*, flourishes in *si-wu*, is entombed in *chen*, and perishes in *xun-si*.
Encountering fire becomes *seal*; wood, *killer*; metal, *depletion*; water, *wealth*; earth, *companion*.

In the four transitional seasons, it is the ruling star; in autumn, it rests; in winter, it is imprisoned; in summer, it is ministerial; in spring, it is restrained.
In years, months, days, or hours of fire or earth, it is imbued with *qi*—auspicious when waxing or flourishing, inauspicious when entombed or perishing.

**Three Green** resides in *Zhen*, its movement belongs to wood. *Yang* wood.
Born in *hai*, declines in *zi*, flourishes in *yin-mao*, is entombed in *wei*, and perishes in *Kun-shen*.
Encountering water becomes *seal*; metal, *killer*; fire, *depletion*; earth, *wealth*; wood, *companion*.
In spring, it is the ruling star; in summer, it rests; in the four transitional seasons, it is imprisoned; in winter, it is ministerial; in autumn, it is restrained.
In years, months, days, or hours of water or wood, it is imbued with *qi*—auspicious when waxing or flourishing, inauspicious when entombed or perishing.

**Four Green** resides in *Xun*, its movement belongs to wood. *Yin* wood.
Some say it is born in reverse in *wu*.
Born in *hai*, declines in *zi*, flourishes in *yin-mao*, is entombed in *wei*, and perishes in *Kun-shen*.
Encountering water becomes *seal*; metal, *killer*; fire, *depletion*; earth, *wealth*; wood, *companion*.
In spring, it is the ruling star; in summer, it rests; in the four transitional seasons, it is imprisoned; in winter, it is ministerial; in autumn, it is restrained.
In years, months, days, or hours of water or wood, it is imbued with *qi*—auspicious when waxing or flourishing, inauspicious when entombed or perishing.

**Five Yellow** resides in the center, its movement belongs to earth. *Neutral* earth.
Born in *shen*, declines in *you*, flourishes in *wu-si*, is entombed in *chen*, and perishes in *Xun-si*.
Encountering fire becomes *seal*; wood, *killer*; metal, *depletion*; water, *wealth*; earth, *companion*.
In the four transitional seasons, it is the ruling star; in autumn, it rests; in winter, it is imprisoned; in summer, it is ministerial; in spring, it is restrained.
In years, months, days, or hours of fire or earth, it is imbued with *qi*—auspicious when waxing or flourishing, inauspicious when entombed or perishing.

**Six White** resides in *Qian*, its movement belongs to metal. *Yang* metal.
Born in *si*, declines in *wu*, flourishes in *shen-you*, is entombed in *chou*, and perishes in *yin-Gen*.
Encountering earth becomes *seal*; fire, *killer*; water, *depletion*; wood, *wealth*; metal, *companion*.
In autumn, it is the ruling star; in winter, it rests; in spring, it is imprisoned; in the four transitional seasons, it is ministerial; in summer, it is restrained.
In years, months, days, or hours of earth or metal, it is imbued with *qi*—auspicious when waxing or flourishing, inauspicious when entombed or perishing.

**Seven Red** resides in *Dui*, its movement belongs to metal. *Yin* metal.
Some say it is born in reverse in *zi*.
Born in *si*, declines in *wu*, flourishes in *shen-you*, is entombed in *chou*, and perishes in *yin-Gen*.
Encountering earth becomes *seal*; fire, *killer*; water, *depletion*; wood, *wealth*; metal, *companion*.
In autumn, it is the ruling star; in winter, it rests; in spring, it is imprisoned; in the four transitional seasons, it is ministerial; in summer, it is restrained.
In years, months, days, or hours of earth or metal, it is imbued with *qi*—auspicious when waxing or flourishing, inauspicious when entombed or perishing.

**Eight White** resides in *Gen*, its movement belongs to earth. *Yang* earth.
Some say it is born in *yin*.
Born in *shen*, declines in *you*, flourishes in *wu-si*, is entombed in *chen*, and perishes in *Xun-si*.
Encountering fire becomes *seal*; wood, *killer*; metal, *depletion*; water, *wealth*; earth, *companion*.
In the four transitional seasons, it is the ruling star; in autumn, it rests; in winter, it is imprisoned; in summer, it is ministerial; in spring, it is restrained.
In years, months, days, or hours of fire or earth, it is imbued with *qi*—auspicious when waxing or flourishing, inauspicious when entombed or perishing.

**Nine Purple** resides in *Li*, its movement belongs to fire.
Born in *yin*, declines in *mao*, flourishes in *si-wu*, is entombed in *xu*, and perishes in *Qian-hai*.
Encountering wood becomes *seal*; water, *killer*; earth, *depletion*; metal, *wealth*; fire, *companion*.
In summer, it is the ruling star; in the four transitional seasons, it rests; in autumn, it is imprisoned; in spring, it is ministerial; in winter, it is restrained.
In years, months, days, or hours of wood or fire, is it imbued with *qi*? Auspicious when waxing or flourishing, inauspicious when entombed or perishing.

Note: The Five Phases (*wuxing*) have examples of *yin* and *yang*, sequential and reverse generation, which are based on the pairing of Heavenly Stems and Earthly Branches. However, among the Nine Palaces’ stars and *sha*, wood, metal, and earth have two each, while water and fire have only one. At the inception of the primordial chaos, only water and fire stood in opposition. Thus, in the *xiantian* (Former Heaven) arrangement, water and fire are placed at the gates of the sun and moon, while in the *houtian* (Later Heaven) arrangement, they establish the solstices of winter and summer. Since water and fire are not duplicated, it is illogical for wood, metal, and earth to be divided into two. Moreover, the authority of *yang* is weighty, while that of *yin* is light; *yin* follows *yang*, embodying the principle of the wife following the husband. Therefore, the waxing, flourishing, entombment, and perishing should not be divided into sequential and reverse patterns.

Furthermore, while it is said that *wu* earth is born in *yin* and *si* earth is born in *you*, this is conventional. According to the fundamental principles of the Five Phases, only earth resides at the junction of fire and metal, between summer and autumn, and only then does it successively generate the myriad things in the four seasons, refining their transformations. Thus, it should rightly be born in *Kun-shen*.

**Exposition on the Diagram of the Nine Palaces’ Purple and White Directions**
In my humble opinion, the ancients’ use of purple and white as auspicious was not without reason. *Six White* resides in *Qian*, the pivot of the Celestial Gate. In terms of time, it is *kai* (opening). *One White* resides in *Kan*, where *yang* *qi* first arises. In terms of time, it is *xiu* (resting). *Eight White* resides in *Gen*, where beginnings and endings are completed. In terms of time, it is *sheng* (generation). *Nine Purple* resides in *Li*, facing the light and governing administration. In terms of time, it is *jing* (prosperity). However, *Three Green* stands in opposition to the sun and moon, while *Seven Red* occupies the realm of stern desolation, bearing the omen of alarm and harm. *Four Green* represents the sprouting of things, yet *Two Black*, transmitting *yin* to send off *yang*, embodies the principle of death and stagnation. *Five Yellow* resides in the center, its position that of the sovereign, its movement that of earth. Its authority governs the four directions, its power overshadows the eight regions—those who encounter it are crushed, those who resist it are destroyed. Thus, among all the baleful stars of the various schools, none is more inauspicious than *Five Yellow*. *Five Yellow* is like the Grand Year (*Taisui*): it may be followed but must not be offended. Such is the fixed positioning of the Nine Stars.

Furthermore, the star of the central palace was named *Taisui* in ancient calendars. Once its position is fixed, *Five Yellow* governs it.

Should the stars wander and drift year by year—now as water, now as wood, now as fire, now as metal—each in turn assumes the role of sovereign. They wield authority over the year, enact the commands of the four seasons, and are not confined to the single *Five Yellow*. The accomplished withdraw, the coming advance: such is the Dao of Heaven. Thus, the star of the central palace bears most critically upon fortune and misfortune each year. For instance, if the orientation of a mountain or dwelling encounters this star, harmony or affinity will mitigate calamity, while conflict or opposition will deepen it. People today know only to avoid *Taisui*, unaware that this star is the true *Taisui*. If the mountain’s orientation aligns with this star, and the year, month, day, and hour further clash with it, the harm will be severe.

When the baleful stars of the Nine Palaces descend upon forbidden positions:
- *Dark Establishment*: a minister usurps the sovereign’s place.
- *Receiving Clash*: the guest weakens, the host strengthens.
- *Mutual Opposition*: the *Piercing Heart* baleful.
- *Metal and Metal in the same position*: the *Crossed Swords* baleful.
- *Metal, Earth, and Wood in the same position*: the *Ox-Fight* baleful.
- *Five Phases entering tomb*: the *Six Victories* baleful.

When selecting a site, establishing an orientation, or modifying a direction, even if *Purple-White* stars are present, their efficacy depends on *qi*: with *qi*, blessings are profound; without *qi*, blessings are slight. One must also consider baleful stars such as *entering tomb*, for "within the auspicious lies the baleful—few recognize this."

The above are but examples of baleful stars to avoid. To grasp their full permutations, one must first correlate the twelve earthly branches with the eight trigrams:
- *Zi* in *Kan*,
- *Chou* and *Yin* in *Gen*,
- *Mao* in *Zhen*, *Chen* in *Xun*,
- *Si* in *Xun*,
- *Wu* in *Li*,
- *Wei* and *Shen* in *Kun*,
- *You* in *Dui*, *Xu* in *Qian*,
- *Hai* in *Qian*.

For instance:
- *One White* flying to *Mao*, *Six White* flying to *Hai*, *Eight White* flying to *Si*, *Nine Purple* flying to *Li*: these are *Punishment Palaces*.
- *One White* flying to *Wu*, *Six White* flying to *Shen*, *Eight White* flying to *Si*, *Nine Purple* flying to *Chou*: these are *Harm Palaces*.

The baleful stars of the Nine Palaces invariably involve the *Three Punishments* and *Six Harms*. One must further examine the year, month, day, and hour to discern the *Four Void* positions, thereby assessing their waxing or waning influence. For example, in the *Jia-Zi* decade, the *Xu-Hai* positions are void. Any beneficent or baleful star aligning with these directions loses power and falls into weakness.

In a *Jia-Zi* year:
- From the first to the eighth month, the *Xu-Hai* positions are void.
- From the ninth to the twelfth month, the *Shen-You* positions are void.

Within the *Jia-Zi* decade, *Xu-Hai* is void, yet on yang days the yang is void, and on yin days the yin is void. The same principle applies to years and months. A single or double void diminishes the star’s power by half; a triple or quadruple void renders it entirely powerless. Generally, a void in the year affects the *qi* of a decade most severely, followed by a void in the month, then the day and hour. Once the void position passes, the star may be employed again.

Beyond punishments, harms, and voids, one must also consider *generation, support, restraint, and transformation*:
- If a *Punishment Palace* aligns with the *Nobleman* or *Office*, punishment transforms into authority.
- If a *Harm Palace* aligns with the *Salary* or *Horse*, harm transforms into utility.

When a void position encounters *generation* or *support*, it becomes substantial; when it encounters *transformation*, it shifts:
- *Generation*: water generates wood, wood generates fire, fire generates earth, earth generates metal, metal generates water, and water again generates wood.
- *Support*: water supports water, wood supports wood, fire supports fire, earth supports earth, metal supports metal.

- *Restraint*: water restrains fire, fire restrains metal, metal restrains wood, wood restrains earth, earth restrains water, and water again restrains fire.
- *Transformation*:
  - By heavenly stems: *Jia* and *Ji* transform into earth, *Yi* and *Geng* into metal, *Bing* and *Xin* into water, *Ding* and *Ren* into wood, *Wu* and *Gui* into fire.
  - By earthly branches: *Hai-Mao-Wei* transform into wood, *Yin-Wu-Xu* into fire, *Si-You-Chou* into metal, *Shen-Zi-Chen* into water.

The transformation of heavenly stems follows the generative and completion numbers of the *River Chart*: one-six, two-seven, three-eight, four-nine, five-ten—these are the natural pairings. The transformation of earthly branches adheres to the native palace of each trigram, where the *qi* of a single palace encompasses birth, prosperity, and tomb—naturally aligning in sequence.

Words cannot exhaust meaning; discernment lies with the adept. Illustrated explanations of the *Three-Yuan Nine-White* system follow.

In the *Upper Yuan* *Jiazi* year, the central palace begins with *One White*. The *Jiazi* year of the Hongzhi seventeenth reign (1484) marks the *Upper Yuan*. In the *Middle Yuan* *Jiazi* year, the central palace begins with *Four Green*. The *Jiazi* year of the Jiajing forty-third reign (1564) marks the *Middle Yuan*. In the *Lower Yuan* *Jiazi* year, the central palace begins with *Seven Red*.

The method of the *Three Yuan* is a system of shifting palaces and exchanging *qi*. This is the wondrous principle of ceaseless cyclical recurrence since the opening of Heaven and Earth. The Dao of the *Yijing* proceeds from one to two, from two to three, and through the interlocking of three and five to generate transformation—how could it not begin from one? *One White* resides in *Kan*, the palace of *Xuanming*, corresponding to the number of *Taiyi* and the root of Heaven in *Fu*. Thus, the *Upper Yuan* *Jiazi* commences here, completing three cycles before returning to this origin—how wondrous! Those who perceive this mechanism are as Shao Yong said: "as if personally witnessing Fu Xi’s arrival."

All subsequent months, days, and hours follow this principle.

**Fixed Palaces of the Three Yuan and Nine White System**
*Upper Yuan*: *Jiazi*, *Yichou*, *Bingyin*, *Dingmao*, *Wuchen*, *Jisi* (The *Jiazi* year of the Hongwu seventieth reign [1384] marks the *Middle Yuan*).
*Middle Yuan*: *Gengwu*, *Xinwei*, *Renshen*, *Guiyou*, *Jiaxu*, *Yihai*; *Bingzi*, *Dingchou*, *Wuyin*, *Jimao*, *Gengchen*, *Xinsi* (The *Jiazi* year of the Zhengtong ninth reign [1444] marks the *Lower Yuan*).
*Lower Yuan*: *Renwu*, *Guiwei*, *Jiashen*, *Yiyou*, *Bingxu*, *Dinghai*; *Wuzhi*, *Jichou*, *Gengyin*, *Xinmao*, *Renchen*, *Guisi* (The *Jiazi* year of the Hongzhi seventeenth reign [1484] marks the *Upper Yuan*).
*Upper Yuan*: *Jiawu*, *Yiwei*, *Bingshen*, *Dingyou*, *Wuxu*, *Jihai*; *Gengzi*, *Xinchou*, *Renyin*, *Guimao*, *Jiachen*, *Yisi* (The *Jiazi* year of the Jiajing forty-third reign [1564] marks the *Middle Yuan*).
*Middle Yuan*: *Bingwu*, *Dingwei*, *Wushen*, *Jiyou*, *Gengxu*, *Xinhai*.
*Lower Yuan*: *Renzi*, *Guichou*, *Jiayin*, *Yimao*, *Bingchen*, *Dingsi*; *Wuwu*, *Jiwei*, *Gengshen*, *Xinyou*, *Renxu*, *Guihai*.

*Upper Yuan*: Green | Red | Central | *Qian* | *Dui* | *Gen* | *Li* | *Kan* | *Kun* | *Zhen* | *Xun*
*Middle Yuan*: Black | Yellow | *Qian* | *Dui* | *Gen* | *Li* | *Kan* | *Kun* | *Zhen* | *Xun* | Central
*Lower Yuan*: Azure | Central | *Dui* | *Gen* | *Li* | *Kan* | *Kun* | *Zhen* | *Xun* | Central | *Qian*
*Upper Yuan*: Green | Red | *Gen* | *Li* | *Kan* | *Kun* | *Zhen* | *Xun* | Central | *Qian* | *Dui*
*Middle Yuan*: Yellow | Black | *Li* | *Kan* | *Kun* | *Zhen* | *Xun* | Central | *Qian* | *Dui* | *Gen*
*Lower Yuan*: Purple | Azure | *Kan* | *Kun* | *Zhen* | *Xun* | Central | *Qian* | *Dui* | *Gen* | *Li*
*Upper Yuan*: Red | Green | *Kun* | *Zhen* | *Xun* | Central | *Qian* | *Dui* | *Gen* | *Li* | *Kan*
*Middle Yuan*: Black | Yellow | *Zhen* | *Xun* | Central | *Qian* | *Dui* | *Gen* | *Li* | *Kan* | *Kun*
*Lower Yuan*: Purple | Azure | White | *Xun* | Central | *Qian* | *Dui* | *Gen* | *Li* | *Kan* | *Kun* | *Zhen*

I observe: regulating the calendar and clarifying the seasons is the primary duty of emperors. Thus, when presenting the coming year’s almanac, a memorial is first composed, and the completed calendar is burned in offering to the Emperor. It is said: "The common people know not how to avoid harm, so the court determines the seasons, dawn and dusk, the auspices of days and months, and promulgates them throughout the realm. Should any error occur in the reckoning of celestial phenomena, the officials shall bear full responsibility, sparing the people from fault."

Yet today’s divination practitioners do not adhere to the court’s regulations but instead peddle secret teachings to the ignorant. Why do they not consider: whose measure of fortune is greater? The court’s or theirs? Whose astronomical calculations are more precise? The court’s specialized officials who observe the heavens and monitor *qi*, or theirs? The officials of the Imperial Bureau of Astronomy have never produced a figure of Yi Xing’s insight or Yelü Chucai’s erudition, yet they act with self-assurance, misleading others profoundly.

The almanac begins with the *Nine White* diagram for the year, followed by detailed monthly diagrams. Diagrams for days and hours are too numerous to record, so they are omitted, awaiting those capable of deducing them by analogy. Alas! The statutes of our dynasty are disregarded, and absurd heterodoxies are often interspersed—how strange and egregious! Thus, I have systematically arranged these principles to facilitate the promotion of orthodoxy and practical application.

**Diagrams of the Three Yuan and Monthly White System**
In *Upper Yuan* years (*Zi-Wu-Mao-You*), the central palace begins with *Eight White* in the first month, *Seven Red* in the second.
In *Middle Yuan* years (*Chen-Xu-Chou-Wei*), the central palace begins with *Five Yellow* in the first month, *Four Green* in the second.
In *Lower Yuan* years (*Yin-Shen-Si-Hai*), the central palace begins with *Two Black* in the first month, *One White* in the second.
All proceed in reverse order, flying sequentially.

Why divide months by the *Three Yuan*? The year after *Zi* is *Chou*, and the year after *Chou* is *Yin*—this is the sequence of *Upper*, *Middle*, and *Lower Yuan*. Why does *Mao* return to the *Upper Yuan*? The *Luo River Writing* contains only nine palaces, and each year has twelve months. Over three years, this totals thirty-six months, matching the number four times nine. The cycle traverses four rounds before returning to the original position. Thus, in the first month of a *Zi* year, *Eight White* begins, and the same occurs in the first month of a *Mao* year. From *Mao* to *Chen* to *Si* to *Wu*, the pattern repeats—this is the ancient method of establishment, and the rest may be deduced by analogy.

**Fixed Palaces of the Three Yuan and Monthly White System**
*Upper Yuan* years (*Zi-Wu-Mao-You*):
First month: 1 | Twelfth month: 2 | First month: 4 | Second: 5 | Third: 6 | Fourth: 7 | Fifth: 8 | Sixth: 9
*Middle Yuan* years (*Chen-Xu-Chou-Wei*):
Seventh: 7 | Eighth: 8 | Ninth: 9 | First month: 1 | Twelfth month: 2 | First month: 4 | Second: 5 | Third: 6
*Lower Yuan* years (*Yin-Shen-Si-Hai*):
Fourth: 4 | Fifth: 5 | Sixth: 6 | Seventh: 7 | Eighth: 8 | Ninth: 9 | First month: 1 | Twelfth month: 2

*One White*: *Dui* | *Gen* | *Li* | *Kan* | *Kun* | *Zhen* | *Xun* | Central | *Qian*
*Two Black*: *Gen* | *Li* | *Kan* | *Kun* | *Zhen* | *Xun* | Central | *Qian* | *Dui*
*Three Azure*: *Li* | *Kan* | *Kun* | *Zhen* | *Xun* | Central | *Qian* | *Dui* | *Gen*
*Four Green*: *Kan* | *Kun* | *Zhen* | *Xun* | Central | *Qian* | *Dui* | *Gen* | *Li*
*Five Yellow*: *Kun* | *Zhen* | *Xun* | Central | *Qian* | *Dui* | *Gen* | *Li* | *Kan*

**Six White**: *Zhen* | *Xun* | Central | *Qian* | *Dui* | *Gen* | *Li* | *Kan* | *Kun*
**Seven Red**: *Xun* | Central | *Qian* | *Dui* | *Gen* | *Li* | *Kan* | *Kun* | *Zhen*
**Eight White**: Central | *Qian* | *Dui* | *Gen* | *Li* | *Kan* | *Kun* | *Zhen* | *Xun*
**Nine Purple**: *Qian* | *Dui* | *Gen* | *Li* | *Kan* | *Kun* | *Zhen* | *Xun* | Central

These are the monthly guiding principles, summarizing the fortunes and misfortunes of the entire year. Their directions are fixed and unchanging, yet their authority, though supreme, is not absolute. As for monthly *shen* and *sha*, the flying and settling of *diaoti*, and their alignment with mountains and orientations—these determine fortune and misfortune most critically. One must clearly understand the methods of weighing their relative importance and making choices.

For instance, according to the *benqi* (original qi) of the Five Phases:
- Wood mountains are auspicious in spring months,
- Fire mountains in summer months,
- Metal mountains in autumn months,
- Water mountains in winter months,
- Earth mountains in the four seasonal months.

According to the *jinqi* (advancing qi) of the Five Phases:
- Wood mountains are auspicious in winter months,
- Fire mountains in spring months,
- Earth mountains in summer months,
- Water mountains in autumn months,
- Metal mountains in the four seasonal months.

According to the *caiqi* (wealth qi) of the Five Phases:
- Metal months are auspicious in spring months,
- Water mountains in summer months,
- Fire mountains in autumn months,
- Earth mountains in winter months,
- Wood mountains in the four seasonal months.

According to the *tuiqi* (retreating qi) of the Five Phases:
- Water mountains are inauspicious in spring months,
- Wood mountains in summer months,
- Earth mountains in autumn months,
- Metal mountains in winter months,
- Fire mountains in the four seasonal months.

According to the *guiqi* (ghost qi) of the Five Phases:
- Earth mountains are inauspicious in spring months,
- Metal mountains in summer months,
- Wood mountains in autumn months,
- Fire mountains in winter months,
- Water mountains in the four seasonal months.

One must also coordinate these with the auspicious and inauspicious aspects of the *zi bai* (Purple-White Stars):
- For Wood mountains, *One White* is favorable as a life-generating star, though its power is weak in spring and the four seasonal months; *Eight White* is favorable as a wealth star, though its power is weak in autumn and spring. *Six White* is inauspicious as a ghost star, but harmless in winter and summer; *Nine Purple* is inauspicious as a draining star, but harmless in the four seasonal months and winter.

- For Water mountains, *Six White* is favorable as a life-generating star, though its power is weak in winter and summer; *Nine Purple* is favorable as a wealth star, though its power is weak in the four seasonal months and winter. *Eight White* is inauspicious as a ghost star, but harmless in autumn and spring.

- For Metal mountains, *Eight White* is favorable as a life-generating star, though its power is weak in autumn and spring; *One White* is inauspicious as a draining star, but harmless in spring and the four seasonal months; *Nine Purple* is inauspicious as a ghost star, but harmless in the four seasonal months and winter.

- For Earth mountains, *Nine Purple* is favorable as a life-generating star, though its power is weak in the four seasonal months and winter; *One White* is favorable as a wealth star, though its power is weak in spring and the four seasonal months. *Six White* is inauspicious as a draining star, but harmless in winter and summer.

- For Fire mountains, *Six White* is favorable as a wealth star, though its power is weak in winter and summer; *One White* is inauspicious as a ghost star, but harmless in spring and the four seasonal months; *Eight White* is inauspicious as a draining star, but harmless in autumn and spring.

Generally, when an auspicious star is restrained or drained, its power weakens; when an inauspicious star is restrained or drained, its malevolence diminishes. One must also coordinate these with the months, the stems and branches of the monthly *jian*, and the *na yin* (sound absorption) to examine their transformations.

For example:
- In a *jiazi* year, *One White* corresponds to *bingzi*, and its *na yin* sound is still considered Water.
- *Six White* corresponds to *yihai*, and its *na yin* sound changes to Fire, thus considered Fire.
- *Eight White* corresponds to *bingyin*, and its *na yin* sound also changes to Fire, thus considered Fire.
- *Nine Purple* corresponds to *gengwu*, and its *na yin* sound changes to Earth, thus considered Earth.

Each year, the *Tai Sui* governs twelve months, each with its designated position, all corresponding to the eight directions. Nowadays, people simplistically assign *One White* to Water, *Six White* to Metal, *Eight White* to Earth, and *Nine Purple* to Fire to determine fortune and misfortune—how can they not be confused when their methods prove ineffective?

In my humble opinion: The transformations of creation exist between Heaven and Earth. The north as Water, south as Fire, east as Wood, and west as Metal are the eternal positions of the Five Phases, their fixed forms. Yet the marvel of their application lies in their yearly divisions, monthly governance, and the ever-changing movements of *diaoti*. As the *Yi Jing* states: *"Change leads to penetration, and penetration leads to endurance."* Without change, how can one speak of the transformations of creation? However, this is merely the most fundamental principle, free from forced interpretations or interruptions. It is for those who understand these principles to deduce and determine their choices.

**Diagram and Explanation of the Three Yuan Daily White Star Sequence**

**Yang Dun after Winter Solstice:**
Twelve *qi*, totaling 180 days, divided into three *yuan*.
- **Upper Yuan:** Winter Solstice, Lesser Cold, Greater Cold, Beginning of Spring.
  *Jiazi* begins with *One White*, *yichou* with *Two Black*.
- **Middle Yuan:** Rain Water, Awakening of Insects, Spring Equinox, Pure Brightness.
  *Jiazi* begins with *Seven Red*, *yichou* with *Eight White*.
- **Lower Yuan:** Grain Rain, Beginning of Summer, Grain Full, Grain in Ear.
  *Jiazi* begins with *Four Green*, *yichou* with *Five Yellow*.

Proceed in order to determine the daily star, starting from the central palace and flying sequentially to the eight directions.

**Yin Dun after Summer Solstice:**
Twelve *qi*, totaling 180 days, divided into three *yuan*.
- **Upper Yuan:** Summer Solstice, Lesser Heat, Greater Heat, Beginning of Autumn.
  *Jiazi* begins with *Nine Purple*, *yichou* with *Eight White*.
- **Middle Yuan:** End of Heat, White Dew, Autumn Equinox, Cold Dew.
  *Jiazi* begins with *Three Azure*, *yichou* with *Two Black*.
- **Lower Yuan:** Frost Descent, Beginning of Winter, Lesser Snow, Greater Snow.
  *Jiazi* begins with *Six White*, *yichou* with *Five Yellow*.

Proceed in reverse order to determine the daily star, starting from the central palace and flying sequentially to the eight directions.

**After Winter Solstice, Yang Dun: Daily White Star Direction Fixed Sequence**
*Jiazi*, *yichou*, *bingyin*, *dingmao*, *wuchen*, *jisi*:
Winter Solstice, Rain Water, Grain Rain
*Gengwu*, *xinwei*, *renshen*, *guiyou*, *jiaxu*, *yihai*:
*Bingzi*, *dingchou*, *wuyin*, *jimao*, *gengchen*, *xinsi*:
Lesser Cold, Awakening of Insects, Beginning of Summer
*Renwu*, *guiwei*, *jiashen*, *yiyou*, *bingxu*, *dinghai*.

**Wuzi, jichou, gengyin, xinmao, renchen, guisi.** *Jiawu, yiwei, bingshen, dingyou, wuxu, jihai.*
Greater Cold, Spring Equinox, Lesser Fullness

**Gengzi, xinchu, renyin, guimao, jiachen, yisi.** *Bingwu, dingwei, wushen, jiyou, gengxu, xinhai.*
Start of Spring, Pure Brightness, Grain in Ear

**Renzi, guichou, jiayin, yimao, bingchen, dingsi.** *Wuwu, jiwei, gengshen, xinyou, renxu, guihai.*
Red, Green Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian
Black, Yellow Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui
Azure, Purple Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen
Green, Red Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li
Yellow, Black Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan
Azure, Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun
Red, Green Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen
Yellow, Black Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun
Azure Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center

This sequence follows the forward order to determine the daily star. The next sequence follows the reverse order. Both enter the central palace and fly sequentially to the eight directions.

**After Summer Solstice, Yin Dun: Daily Dark Star Direction Fixed Sequence**
*Jiazi, yichou, bingyin, dingmao, wuchen, jisi:*
Summer Solstice, End of Heat, Frost Descent
*Gengwu, xinwei, renshen, guiyou, jiaxu, yihai:*
*Bingzi, dingchou, wuyin, jimao, gengchen, xinsi:*
Lesser Heat, White Dew, Start of Winter
*Renwu, guiwei, jiashen, yiyou, bingxu, dinghai:*
Greater Heat, Autumn Equinox, Lesser Snow
*Wuzu, jichou, gengyin, xinmao, renchen, guisi:*
Frost Descent, Cold Dew, Greater Snow
*Bingwu, dingwei, wushen, jiyou, gengxu, xinhai:*
Azure Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian
Black Yellow Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui
Red Green Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen
Azure Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li
Yellow Black Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun
Green Red Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen
Azure Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun
Black Yellow Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center
Green Red Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center

As Chen Xiyi’s *Key to the Three Yuan for Day Selection* states:
*"Yang arises before and after Winter Solstice, moving forward with *jiazi* one palace at a time.
At Rain Water, begin from the seventh palace; at Grain Rain, return to reckon from Xun.
Yin arises after Summer Solstice, shifting through the nine palaces.
Before and after End of Heat, doubt not the third palace.
At Frost Descent, *jiazi* begins from the sixth palace—
Reverse and forward are clear in the twelve branches."*

For the various methods of daily White Stars, confusion and errors abound.
Only this *Three Yuan Day Selection Formula* maintains the continuity of yin-yang and forward-reverse sequences, perfectly preserving the ancient principle of "shifting palaces to connect with the qi."

The most critical factor is the day’s ruler, which must correlate usefully with the mountain’s destiny.
For example, in spring, *wu* and *ji* are weak and useless; in the *yin* month, *si* days suffer triple punishment; in the *mao* month, *chen* days endure six harms. Opposing the Grand Year is called "great defeat."
*Chou* days in the *wei* month are always inauspicious.
Days of "eating, submission, extinction, and disappearance" are especially unfavorable—even with Purple-White stars, they bring no good.

**Diagram and Explanation of Three Yuan Hourly White Star Sequence**

**After Winter Solstice, Yang Dun:** Change sequence every five days, dividing into two yuan. (Old texts placed the middle yuan at *chen-xu-chou-wei*; this is corrected.)
- **Upper Yuan:** On *jia* or *ji* days meeting *zi-wu-mao-you*, begin with *One White* at *jiazi*.
- **Middle Yuan:** On *jia* or *ji* days meeting *yin-shen-si-hai*, begin with *Seven Red* at *jiazi*.
- **Lower Yuan:** On *jia* or *ji* days meeting *chen-xu-chou-wei*, begin with *Four Green* at *jiazi*.
All proceed in forward order to determine the hourly star, entering the central palace and flying sequentially to the eight directions.

**After Summer Solstice, Yin Dun:** Change sequence every five days, dividing into three yuan. (Old texts placed the middle yuan at *chen-xu-chou-wei*; this is corrected.)
- **Upper Yuan:** On *jia* or *ji* days meeting *zi-wu-mao-you*, begin with *Nine Purple* at *jiazi*.
- **Middle Yuan:** On *jia* or *ji* days meeting *yin-shen-si-hai*, begin with *Three Azure* at *jiazi*.
- **Lower Yuan:** On *jia* or *ji* days meeting *chen-xu-chou-wei*, begin with *Six White* at *jiazi*.
All proceed in reverse order to determine the hourly star, entering the central palace and flying sequentially to the eight directions.

**After Winter Solstice, Yang Dun: Hourly White Star Direction Fixed Sequence**
(All begin at *jiazi*, not the Five-Child Rotation. Old texts contain errors.)

One White: Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian
Two Black: Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui
Three Azure: Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen
Four Green: Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li
Five Yellow: Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan

**Six White:** Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun
**Seven Red:** Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen
**Eight White:** Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun
**Nine Purple:** Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center

*Note:* Common almanacs fix the hourly White Star by taking *chen-xu-chou-wei* as the Middle Yuan and *yin-shen-si-hai* as the Lower Yuan, which is gravely erroneous. The ancients established the Three Yuan method such that the Nine Palaces’ flying sequence must complete three *jiazi* cycles before returning to the original position. For instance, if the first *jiazi* begins at *One Kan*, the second *jiazi* naturally begins at *Seven Dui*, and the third *jiazi* at *Four Xun*—a fixed, interlocking system. The later sequence of reverse *dun* (Yang *dun* after Winter Solstice begins at *Li*) follows the same principle. Taking *chen-xu-chou-wei* as the Middle Yuan contradicts this method.

**After Summer Solstice, Yin Dun: Hourly White Star Direction Fixed Sequence**
(All begin at *jiazi*, not the Five-Child Rotation. Old texts contain errors.)

**Nine Purple:** Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian
**Eight White:** Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui
**Seven Red:** Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen
**Six White:** Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li
**Five Yellow:** Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun Kan
**Six White:** Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen Kun
**Seven Red:** Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun Zhen
**Eight White:** Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center Xun
**Nine Purple:** Xun Zhen Kun Kan Li Gen Dui Qian Center

*Further Note:* The practice of taking *chen-xu-chou-wei* as the Middle Yuan stems from erroneously applying the monthly White Star method to hourly calculations, perpetuating the mistake. The ancients devised this shortcut to avoid the cumbersome task of tallying accumulated years and days in the celestial cycle. For monthly White Stars, the *zi* year is the Upper Yuan, so the *chou* year becomes the Middle Yuan—since the twelfth month of the *zi* year directly precedes the first month of the *chou* year. For example, in the twelfth month of the *zi* year, *Six White* occupies the central palace; thus, in the first month of the *chou* year, *Five Yellow* advances to replace it. This is the method of matching twelve palaces with nine palaces. However, hourly White Stars must traverse all sixty *jiazi* cycles, with each Yuan changing every five days. If the sequence begins on a *jiazi* day, the *jiazi* hour must wait until the *ji-si* day to complete a full cycle—meaning the *zi* day is the Upper Yuan, and the *si* day should be the Middle Yuan, a system of matching sixty hours with nine palaces. Moreover, the Yin and Yang *dun* differ in forward and reverse sequences, diverging significantly from the monthly method and violating logic. Here, corrections are made. For instance, if the monthly method starts with *jiazi* on the first day, the next day should be *bingzi*, not another *jiazi*. If *One White* is placed sequentially on the first day, the next day should be *Four Green*, not *Seven Red*. If *Nine Purple* is placed in reverse on the first day, the next day should be *Six White*, not *Three Azure*. Only then does it align with the twelve-palace calculation method. Otherwise, how could the *zi* day be the Upper Yuan and the *chou* day the Middle Yuan?

---

**Outline of the Tai Sui Single Star Method**

The Tai Sui single star brings calamities hard to guard,
All inauspicious stars and dangers cannot be withstood.
Simply calculate the Three Yuan’s own sequence,
Those who offend it will suffer heavy mourning in their homes.

The Tai Sui single star—who does not know?
Within each year lies a time of misfortune.
Its monthly progression is most subtle,
With no fixed pattern or constant rule.

For example, in the Upper Yuan *jiazi* year,
*One White* arrives at the palace and flies to the nine heavens.
At *Zi*, *Six* is obtained again in the palace,
Then returning to *Li*—words cannot describe the dread.

The method: Place the Three Yuan’s annual star in the central palace, then locate the Tai Sui’s own palace. The star found there is moved to the central palace to determine the annual star’s position. The annual star is the star of the central palace for that year, hence called the Tai Sui single star.

For instance, in the Upper Yuan *jiazi* year, *One White* enters the central palace. Counting forward to the Tai Sui’s position at *Kan*, *Six White* is obtained. Then place *Six White* in the central palace and locate *One White* at *Li*. *Li* contains the character *Wu* (午). Check which palace *Wu* falls into each month, then trace *One White* alongside *Wu*—this is the true Tai Sui single star.

Modern practitioners mistakenly name the opposite of Tai Sui as the "broken year" position, but this is not the single star.

- *Zi* year: Tai Sui at *Kan*
- *Chou* and *Yin* years: Tai Sui at *Gen*
- *Mao* year: Tai Sui at *Zhen*
- *Chen* and *Si* years: Tai Sui at *Xun*
- *Wu* year: Tai Sui at *Li*
- *Wei* and *Shen* years: Tai Sui at *Kun*
- *You* year: Tai Sui at *Dui*
- *Xu* and *Hai* years: Tai Sui at *Qian*

Trace the palace monthly to discern the inauspicious period,
Always beware of the Tai Sui’s relentless pursuit.
For example, if *One White* resides at *Li*,
In the second month, it moves to *Gen* to offend it.

For instance, in the Upper Yuan *jiazi* year, the second month is *ding-mao*. Move *Mao* to the central palace and locate *Wu* at *Gen*.

- In *zi-wu-mao-you* years:
  - First month: *Eight White* starts in the central palace
  - Second month: *Seven Red* starts in the central palace
  - Sequential flight: *Eight White* → *Qian* → *Nine Purple* → *Dui* → *One White*, then to *Gen*, where the monthly *Wu* also arrives—most inauspicious.

**Water-Fire Tai Sui: What harm does it bring?**
It surely causes heavy mourning and sparks of war.
For example, in the Upper Yuan *jiazi* year, *One White* is the Tai Sui single star. In the third month, *Six White* is in the central palace, and *One White* flies to *Li*—water entering the fire region, heralding heavy mourning.

**Water-Metal Tai Sui: What misfortune does it bring?**
Lust and chaos in the inner chambers, disasters abound.
Wives are harmed, elders lost—suffering is vast.
For example, in the Upper Yuan *jiazi* year, *One White* is the Tai Sui. In the first month, *Eight White* is in the central palace, and *One White* flies to *Dui*—water entering the metal palace, bringing lust and disorder.

**Kan** governs the middle son, thus it presides over misfortunes in the central chamber. When the Tai Sui occupies a direction, one is not free—water and earth bring pestilence and pox as harbingers of sorrow.
For example, in the Upper Yuan *jiazi* year, in the second month, *Seven Red* resides in the central palace, and *One White* flies sequentially to *Gen*—this is the Tai Sui of water and earth, presiding over epidemics.

Water and fire bring loss of wealth and self-hanging; when water and fire meet, snakes and dogs grieve.
For example, in the Upper Yuan *jiazi* year, in the seventh month, *Two Black* is in the central palace, and *One White* flies to *Xun*—water entering the wood region. In the fourth month, *Five Yellow* is in the central palace, and *One White* flies to *Kan*—water entering the water region.
The aforementioned afflictions, if not accompanied by punishment or combination, do not result in major disasters.

Fire and wood bring grievous harm through punishment and injury; fire and metal, though productive, harm the fetus.
Fire and earth bring illness and early death; water and fire further harm infants.
Wood and water bring wind-borne harm and violent death; wood and metal lead to imprisonment and death.
Wood and earth cause fractures and abscesses; wood and fire bring harm swift as a blade.
Metal and metal bring short lives and violent ends; wood and wood bring goiters and epilepsy.
Earth and earth bring blindness and muteness—these are the interconnected principles of the Five Phases’ afflictions.

I urge you to further employ the transformations of the *Diao* palace, and the auspicious and inauspicious will be clearly before your eyes.
The above discusses the general judgments of the Tai Sui single star, illustrating the mechanisms of the Five Phases’ resonances.
From this, it is evident that the mutual generation, conquest, restraint, and transformation of the Nine Stars do not depart from the waxing and waning of the Five Phases and the eight directions. All calculations ultimately return to a single principle: the year and month serve as the outline, though weighty, while the day and hour act as the pivot—no small matter indeed.
Further integrating the cyclical movements of *yunqi* and the permutations of *qimen*, then all unfounded precedents may be discarded, and baseless heterodoxies will crumble of themselves.
Mencius said: *"When the classics are rectified, the people will be free from depravity."* Are not the books of the *He* and *Luo* the very classics for extinguishing heterodoxy?
Though I am not talented, I have arranged these discussions in order as above, awaiting those who come after.

*End of Volume Six of* **The Confucian School’s Esteem for Principle: A Balanced Compilation of Kan Yu and Filial Piety**
*Beginning of Volume Seven of* **The Confucian School’s Esteem for Principle: A Balanced Compilation of Kan Yu and Filial Piety**

**Introduction to the Five Stars and Fate**
*Kanyu* fate-calculation is the same as Five-Star fate-divination. Five-Star fate-divination emphasizes the auspiciousness or inauspiciousness of stellar bodies to determine fortune or misfortune. *Kanyu* fate-calculation also examines the auspiciousness or inauspiciousness of stellar bodies to guide avoidance or pursuit. The difference is that astrologers additionally weigh the *caigong* (Palace of Wealth), whereas fate-calculation does not. Astrologers may establish the body and fate in *Mao*, while fate-calculation does so based on the hour employed—this is a minor distinction. Nevertheless, the principles of astrology should not be ignored, hence I have compiled this brief introduction.

**Palace Divisions and Their Correspondences**
*Bin* and *Ping* share the green position,
*Mo* and *Jie* extend to Yangzhou.
*Renma* resides in Yan and You,
*Tianjie* seeks Song and Yu.
*Tianping* divides Zheng and Yan,
*Shuangnü* governs Chu and Keqiu.
The Three Rivers and Zhou belong to *Shizi*,
*Juxie* lingers in Qin and Yong.
*Yi* and *Wei* occupy the Yin-Yang positions,
*Zhaoyi* is the Metal Ox.
*Baiyang* rules Lu and Xu,
*Shuangyu* gathers Wei and Bin.

**Degrees and Their Correspondences**
Wood *Jiao*: twelve degrees,
Metal *Long*: nine degrees.
Earth *Mo*: sixteen degrees,
Sun *Tu*: five attributes.
Six Lunar Mansions:
Moon *Hu*: eighteen degrees,
Fire *Hu*.
Water *Bao*: nine degrees,
twenty-four degrees for Wood *Ban*.
Metal *Niu*: six degrees,
ten degrees for Earth *Fu*.
Nine Degrees:
Sun *Shu*,
Moon *Yan*: fifteen degrees.
Fire *Du*: seventeen degrees,
Water *Yu*: nine degrees.
Seventeen degrees for Wood *Lang*,
*Lou* and Metal *Gou*: twelve degrees.
Earth *Zhi*: fifteen degrees,
*Mao* and Sun *Ji*: ten degrees.
Sixteen Degrees:
Moon *Wu*,
Fire *Hou*: one and a half degrees.
Water *Yuan*: nine degrees,
Water *Gan*: thirty-two degrees.
Metal *Niu*: twelve degrees,
*Liu* and Earth *Zhang*.
Sun *Ma*: six degrees,
Moon *Lu*: sixteen degrees.
Fire *She*: nineteen degrees,
Water *Yin*: seventeen degrees.

**Degrees and Their Positions**
Initially, all reside in *Xin*,
the second in *Cun*.
The third in *Wei*,
the fourth in the true palace.
The second also resides in *Zi*,
thirteen degrees in the moving palace.
All reside in *Xu*,
the second in the intimate palace.
The fourth also traverses *Jing*,
seven degrees in *Jing*.
Nine all reside in *Shen*,
four degrees in *Ying*.
Fifteen degrees,
ten return to *Zi*.

**Degrees of the Sun’s Movement**
At *Lichun*, it begins at one degree,
at *Yushui*, it seeks seven.
At *Jingzhe*, six degrees,
at *Chunfen*, it roams three.
At *Qingming*, it descends nine,
at *Guyu*, it lingers six.
At *Lixia*, it edges eight,
at *Xiaoman*, it gathers eight.
At *Mangzhong*, eleven degrees,
at *Xiazhi*, nine at the head.
At *Xiaoshu*, thirteen degrees,
at *Dashu*, twenty-nine.
At *Liqiu*, *Liu* at ten degrees,
at *Chushu*, five are present.
At *Bailu*, two stand,
at *Qiufen*, seventeen.
At *Hanlu*, thirteen degrees,
at *Shuangjiang*, ten are reached.
At *Lidong*, two proceed,
at *Xiaoxue*, two arrive.
At *Daxue*, six approach,
at *Dongzhi*, four press close.
At *Xiaohan*, ten connect,
at *Dahan*, the Ox holds two straight.

**Degrees of the Moon’s Movement**
To know the degrees of the Moon’s movement,
its nodes begin at *Wei*.
Each day it travels thirteen degrees,
shifting through two palaces every three days.
*Kui* and *Wei* follow *Bi*,
*Jing* and *Liu* dwell in *Zhang*.
The Moon takes *Yi* as its starting point,
*Jiao* and *Kang* as its journey.
The Moon takes *Fang* as its origin,
*Jian* and *Ji* are carefully sought.
The Moon’s *Qianniu* must be known,
its degrees in the celestial cycle are precise.

**Morning and Evening Degrees**
Evening degrees begin at *You*; for those born from the first to the fifteenth or sixteenth day, count from *You*, advancing one degree per hour. For *You*, *Xu*, and *Hai*, count forward; for *Shen*, *Wei*, *Wu*, *Si*, *Chen*, *Mao*, *Yin*, *Chou*, and *Zi*, count backward.
Morning degrees begin at *Mao*; for those born from the fifteenth or sixteenth to the thirtieth day, count from *Mao*, advancing one degree per hour. For *Mao*, *Chen*, *Si*, *Wu*, *Wei*, *Shen*, *You*, *Xu*, and *Hai*, count forward; for *Yin*, *Chou*, and *Zi*, count backward.

From the first to the fourth day, the Moon moves most swiftly, traversing over fourteen degrees in a day and night. From the fifth to the eighth day, the Moon’s motion is moderate, traversing over thirteen degrees in a day and night. From the ninth to the nineteenth day, the Moon moves slowly, traversing over twelve degrees in a day and night. From the twentieth to the twenty-third day, the Moon moves with slight swiftness, traversing over thirteen degrees in a day and night. From the twenty-fourth to the thirtieth day, the Moon moves with great swiftness, traversing over fourteen degrees in a day and night.

**Degrees of Celestial Bodies**
The Sun traverses one degree per day, one palace per month, and completes one celestial cycle in a year. The Moon traverses thirteen degrees per day, one palace every two and a half days, and completes one celestial cycle in a month. Jupiter moves forward, traversing one degree every five days, one palace per year, and completes one celestial cycle in twelve years. Mars moves forward, traversing one degree every half day, one palace every two months, and completes one celestial cycle in two years. Saturn moves forward, traversing one degree every ten days, one palace every twenty-eight months, and completes one celestial cycle in twenty-eight years. Venus moves forward, traversing one degree per day, one palace per month, and completes one celestial cycle in a year. Mercury moves forward, traversing one degree per day, one palace per month, and completes one celestial cycle in a year. The Purple Qi traverses one degree every twenty-nine days, one palace every twenty-nine months, and completes one celestial cycle in twenty-nine years. The Comet traverses one degree every nine days, one palace every nine months, and completes one celestial cycle in nine years. Rahu and Ketu traverse one degree every eighteen days, one palace every eighteen months, and complete one celestial cycle in eighteen years.

Of the nine celestial bodies—the Sun, Moon, Jupiter, Mars, Saturn, Venus, Mercury, *qi*, and Comet—all move forward in degrees but backward in palaces. Only Rahu and Ketu move forward in palaces but backward in degrees.

Whenever Jupiter, Mars, Saturn, Venus, or Mercury exhibit phases of slowness, station, concealment, or retrogradation, their appearances at dawn and dusk must be carefully examined. Among these, the Moon’s degrees are particularly noted: after the new moon, it follows the evening degrees; after the full moon, it follows the morning degrees. These must be meticulously calculated.

**Method for Determining the Life Palace**
The Moon is the body star. The degree where the Moon resides becomes the master of one’s body degree. Add the birth hour to the Sun’s palace, counting forward until reaching *Mao*, which is the Life Palace. For example, if the Sun is in the *Zi* palace and the person is born at the *You* hour, add the *You* hour to the *Zi* palace and count forward to *Wu*, where *Mao* is encountered—this is the Life Palace. Since the Sun rises at *Mao*, *Mao* is designated as the Life Palace. The degree of the Sun opposite the degree of the Life Palace is the Life Degree. For instance, if the Sun resides at six degrees in the *Xu* palace, it opposes five degrees in the *Wu* palace—this is the Life Degree. If the Sun resides at three degrees in the *Nü* palace, it opposes four degrees in the *Liu* mansion—this is the Life Degree. The rest follow this example.

**The Twelve Palaces**
Life Palace, Wealth, Siblings, Property, Children, Servants, Spouse, Illness, Migration, Career, Blessings, Appearance.

To determine the twelve palaces, count backward in rotation. For example, if the Life Palace is in *Yin*, Wealth is in *Si*, Siblings in *Zi*, Property in *Hai*, Children in *Xu*, Servants in *You*, Spouse in *Shen*, Illness in *Wei*, and so forth.

**Method for Determining the Annual Limit**
The annual limit is determined by the palace and position of the Life Degree. For example, if the Life Degree is at five degrees in the *Xing* mansion, located in the fifth position of the *Wu* palace on the star chart, the annual limit begins at fifteen years. If the Life Degree is at three, four, or five degrees, the annual limit begins at eleven years. If the Life Degree is at eleven, twelve, or thirteen degrees in the *Zhang* mansion, the annual limit begins at twenty years.

Generally, the annual limit starts as early as eleven years or as late as twenty years. Counting from the degrees on the star chart is more convenient, though the *Liangtianchi* (measuring celestial ruler) is more precise.

**Verses on Annual Divisions**
Fifteen and ten,
Eleven is clear.
Fifteen is the highest position,
Only eight years of provisions remain.
Seven and six times six,
Five years strong.
Sum them,
Four and a half years settle the minutest details.

**Verses on Degrees of Motion**
Degrees of motion vary in depth,
Three degrees stand in one year.
Two degrees pass in one year,
Three years together make ten.
A year with four degrees strong,
Three years above add one more.
Three degrees shift,
Three years subtract one as the standard.
Sum them,
One year with seven degrees, subtract one.
Each five years,
A year with six degrees proceeds without fail.
If one can follow this discourse on annual motion,
Fortune and misfortune will be clearly known year by year.

The above methods for determining limits and years follow the preceding examples. However, the ancient method of a fifteen-year Life Palace should not be rigidly adhered to. For those whose annual limit begins at eleven, the Life Palace governs only ten years, or three additional degrees, as one degree is traversed every three years. For those whose annual limit begins at twenty, the Life Palace governs nineteen years, approximately twenty-six or twenty-seven degrees, as one degree is traversed every year and a half. The rest can be inferred similarly.

The depth of the Life Palace’s degrees and the degrees traversed by the annual limit are called the *Liangtianchi*. The Life Palace above and the *Liangtianchi* are both fixed methods for determining fate. The Life Palace is found by adding the *Mao* hour to the Sun’s palace and degree, then counting to the birth hour. The *Liangtianchi* is found by adding the birth hour to the Sun’s palace and degree, then counting to *Mao*. Though the counting methods differ, their essence is the same. Examining each palace is cumbersome; the *Liangtianchi* offers a swift and convenient method—using it alone is sufficient.

As the *Liangtianchi* method determines fate by fixed nodal points, it cannot account for every initial degree, so discrepancies of one or two degrees may occur. Only by cross-referencing with the calculations for each palace can precision to the minute and second be achieved.

The time of birth used by astrologers is the same as that employed by geomancers—this should not be rigidly adhered to.

**Methods of Observation**

**Stars**
Stars refer to the Sun, Moon, Jupiter, Mars, Saturn, Venus, Mercury, *qi*, Comet, *Rāhu*, *Ketu*, as well as the Literary Brilliance, Named Stem, Official Seal, Warp-and-Weft, Post Horse, Three Origins, Four Origins, Promotion Catalyst, Emolument Spirit, Auspicious Spirit, Rank, Ten *Yu*, and Transformative Luminaries.

**Malefics**
Malefics refer to the Emolument Effort, Yearly Chariot, Heavenly One, Jade Hall, Dipper Handle, Hexagram *Qi*, Tang Talisman, State Seal, as well as the Yang Blade, Sword Edge, Heavenly Male, Earthly Female, Flying Lament, Precise Killer, Death Spirit, Four Wastes, and Four Talismans.

**Palaces**
Palaces and their rulers: *Zi* and *Chou* Palaces (Earth), *Yin* and *Hai* Palaces (Wood), *Mao* and *Xu* Palaces (Fire), *Chen* and *You* Palaces (Metal), *Si* and *Shen* Palaces (Water), *Wu* Palace (Sun), and *Wei* Palace (Moon).

**Degrees**
Degrees and their rulers: *Jiao*, *Dou*, *Kui*, and *Jing* Degrees (Water); *Kang*, *Niu*, *Lou*, and *Gui* Degrees (Metal); *Di*, *Nü*, *Wei*, and *Liu* Degrees (Earth); *Fang*, *Xu*, *Mao*, and *Xing* Degrees (Sun); *Xin*, *Wei*, *Bi*, and *Zhang* Degrees (Moon); *Wei*, *Shi*, *Zi*, and *Yi* Degrees (Fire); *Ji*, *Bi*, *Shen*, and *Zhen* Degrees (Water).

**Strong Palaces**
Strong palaces include the Life Palace, Official Emolument, Fields and Dwellings, Spouses and Concubines, Children, Blessings and Virtue, and Wealth. It is also said that Wealth is slightly weaker, as it opposes the Life Palace.

**Weak Palaces**
Weak palaces include Siblings, Servants, Illness and Calamity, Appearance, and Migration. It is also said that Migration is nearly strong, as it faces the Life Palace.

**Body**
The *Body* is static. It is also called the original fixed star chart, upon which the Seven Governors and Four Remainders are arranged. It governs the body, life, official rank, blessings, fields, wealth, spouse, descendants, Literary Brilliance, Warp-and-Weft, Three Origins, Four Origins, and other stars.

**Use**
The *Use* is dynamic. It also refers to the movement through the celestial degrees, governing the Greater and Lesser Limits, the annual flow of the Eleven Luminaries, the Year Star, and the distribution of palaces and malefics.

**Engendering**
Engendering is mutual generation. Wood engenders Fire, Fire engenders Earth, Earth engenders Metal, Metal engenders Water, and Water engenders Wood. For stars governing the body, life, official rank, blessings, fields, wealth, spouse, and descendants, it is auspicious when others come to engender me.

**Restriction**
Restriction is mutual restraint. Wood restricts Earth, Earth restricts Water, Water restricts Fire, Fire restricts Metal, and Metal restricts Wood. For stars governing the body, fields, wealth, spouse, descendants, official rank, and blessings, it is strictly forbidden when others come to restrict me.

**Control**
Control is a form of restraint. When Metal restricts Wood, Fire controls it; when Fire restricts Metal, Water controls it; when Water restricts Fire, Earth controls it; when Earth restricts Water, Wood controls it; when Wood restricts Earth, Metal controls it.

**Transformation**
Transformation is a form of generation. When Metal restricts Wood, Water transforms it; when Water restricts Fire, Wood transforms it; when Wood restricts Earth, Fire transforms it; when Fire restricts Metal, Earth transforms it; when Earth restricts Water, Metal transforms it.

**Opposition**
Opposition is mutual reflection. *Zi* and *Wu* oppose each other, *Chou* and *Wei* oppose each other, *Yin* and *Shen* oppose each other, *Mao* and *You* oppose each other, *Chen* and *Xu* oppose each other, and *Si* and *Hai* oppose each other. If the opposition is auspicious, it is auspicious; if inauspicious, it is inauspicious.

**Harmony**
Harmony is mutual convergence. *Shen*, *Zi*, and *Chen* converge; *Yin*, *Wu*, and *Xu* converge; *Si*, *You*, and *Chou* converge; *Hai*, *Mao*, and *Wei* converge. If the convergence is auspicious, it is auspicious; if inauspicious, it is inauspicious.

**Facing**
Facing refers to the orientation of stars. For example, the Sun and Moon facing, official rank and blessings facing, fields and wealth facing, Literary Brilliance facing, Warp-and-Weft facing, Three Origins and Four Origins facing, or a single dominant star facing.

**Turning Away**
Turning away refers to the retreat of multiple luminaries. For instance, when *Ketu* and *Rāhu* intercept stars in the southeast while the fate limit passes through the northwest, or when they intercept stars in the northwest while the fate limit lies in the southeast. It is also when the Sun and Moon turn away, and all stars sink into obscurity.

**Before and After**
There are two perspectives on before and after.

Just as the *Zi* palace serves as the center, the *Chou* palace is before it and the *Hai* palace behind—this defines the "before and after" of palaces. When *Jiao* degrees serve as the center, *Kang* degrees are before and *Zhen* degrees behind—this defines the "before and after" of degrees. In fate-limit analysis, the "before and after" of palaces determine fortune or misfortune. In stellar configurations, the "before and after" of degrees settle blessings or calamities. There are also distinctions of "before and after" within the same palace, as well as within the same degree.

**After**
The *Classic* states: When the Sun and Moon occupy the same palace, the Moon must be positioned before the Sun. For example, the Moon in *Jing* and the Sun in *Bi*. It also says: When Venus and Mercury meet in the same enclosure, Mercury must not retreat behind Venus. For instance, Mercury in *Jing* and Venus in *Bi*. There are also distinctions of "before and after" in mutual overcoming. If Earth is in *Jing* and Water in *Bi*, the misfortune is light. If Earth is in *Bi* and Water in *Jing*, the misfortune is grave. Generally, stars that generate me should be behind, while stars that overcome me should be before. The rest can be deduced accordingly.

**Welcoming**
"Welcoming" means a star lies ahead. For example, if the fate limit is in *Yin* and a star is in *Mao*, this is called "inter-palace welcoming." If the fate limit is in *Ji* and a star is in *Wei* degrees, this is called "inter-degree welcoming." The former is minor, the latter significant.

**Sending Off**
"Sending off" means a star lies behind. For example, if the fate limit is in *Yin* and a star is in *Chou*, this is called "inter-palace sending off." If the fate limit is in *Ji* and a star is in *Wei* degrees, this is called "inter-degree sending off." The former is distant, the latter proximate.

**Bright**
"Bright" refers to stars that align with daylight or night. For those born in daylight: the Sun, Jupiter, Saturn, Mercury, *qi*, *Ketu*, and *comets*. For those born at night: the Moon, Mars, Venus, and *Rāhu*—these are called "facing brightness." When they govern the body, fate, fields, wealth, official blessings, warp-and-weft, post horses, the Three Origins, or emolument stars, they are considered auspicious.

**Obscure**
"Obscure" refers to stars that oppose daylight or night. For those born at night: Jupiter, Saturn, Mercury, *darkness*, *Ketu*, and *comets*. For those born in daylight: the Moon, Mars, Venus, and *Rāhu*—these are called "turning away from luminaries." Or when they govern the body, fate, fields, wealth, or official blessings, and stars like Literary Brilliance or *Ming Jia* lose their proper positions.

**Ascending**
"Ascending" means the Sun is in the east, favoring those born in *Yin*, *Mao*, *Chen*, *Si*, *Wu*, or *Wei* hours. The Moon is in the west, favoring those born in *Shen*, *You*, *Xu*, *Hai*, *Zi*, or *Chou*.

**Sinking**
"Sinking" means the Sun is in the west for night births, or the Moon is in the east for day births. When governing official blessings, the body, fate, fields, wealth, or spouses and heirs, this is called "the Sun losing its configuration."

**Sequential**
"Sequential" means the Five Stars move from north to west, or from south to east, following degrees in mutual generation without discordant stars—this is auspicious. For example, Wood, Fire, Earth, Metal, and Water generating in sequence is propitious.

**Reversed**
"Reversed" means the Five Stars move from north to east, or from south to west, clashing in mutual overcoming, with chaotic stars—this is inauspicious. For example, Water, Fire, Metal, Wood, and Earth clashing in conflict is ominous.

**Declining**
"Declining" refers to Earth in spring, Metal in summer, Wood in autumn, Fire in winter, and Water in the four transitional seasons. Additionally, stars in states of decline, illness, death, extinction, gestation, or nurturing are in decline. When governing stars occupy such positions, it is especially unfavorable.

**Prosperous**
"Prosperous" refers to Wood in spring, Fire in summer, Metal in autumn, Water in winter, and Earth in the four transitional seasons. Additionally, stars in states of growth, maturity, or peak power are prosperous. When governing stars occupy such positions, it is especially auspicious.

**Concealing**
"Concealing" refers to *Rāhu* and *Ketu* obscuring stars. They may conceal stars in the northwest by day or hide luminaries in the southeast by night.

**Eclipsing**
